Quranic Proofs that the Name of Iman Remains Despite Major Sins
Maturidi cites multiple Qur'anic verses as proof that major sinners retain the name 'believers'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Qur'anic verses to argue that major sins do not remove the name of faith (iman) from a believer.

Core Idea
The Qur'an addresses sinners as 'believers,' proving the name of iman remains.

Maturidi presents a series of Qur'anic proofs to counter the view that major sins erase the name of iman. Each verse addresses sinners with 'O you who have believed' even while rebuking them for grave sins. This lesson examines these verses and Maturidi's reasoning that the continued use of the term 'believers' indicates that the name of faith remains despite the sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage and then its English translation. Notice how each verse begins with 'O you who have believed' even when rebuking a sin.
The pattern is consistent across all verses.
2
Identify the sin in each verse
For each verse cited by Maturidi, identify the sin being addressed (e.g., saying what you don't do, fighting, murder, etc.).
Some sins are major, like murder.
3
Understand Maturidi's reasoning
Maturidi argues that if these sins removed one from iman, Allah would not have addressed them as believers. Reflect on this logic and why it is a strong proof.
This is the core of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن الله سبحانه أبقى له اسم الإيمان مع تحقيق ما عليه الوعيد في حكمه بقوله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لِمَ تَقُولُونَ مَا لَا تَفْعَلُونَ، فأوجب فيه المقت عنده مع اسم الإيمان بحرف العتاب الذي لا يحتمل النطق قبل مقارفة الذنب بقوله: لِمَ تَقُولُونَ، والمقت لا يوجب الذنب الذي في الحكمة لزوم المغفرة له، وقال: وَإِنْ طَائِفَتَانِ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ اقْتَتَلُوا، أثبت لهم اسم الإيمان الزام اسم البغي لأحدهما في القتال، وألزم من حضر موته المبغى عليه حتى الآخر إلى أمر الله، ولو كان ذلك خروج من الإيمان لكان الحق في مثل ذلك غير الذي ذكر. وقال: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ القِصَاصُ في القَتْلَى، ومعلوم أنه لا يجب إلا بقتل العمد، فأثبت لهم في ابتداء الآية اسم الإيمان، وأبقى بينها الأخوة، وأخبر أن ذلك تخفيف من ربكم ورحمة، وتبعد هذه الأوصاف فيمن أخرجهم الفعل من الإيمان. وقال: وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَلَمْ يُهَاجِرُوا مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ وِلَايَتِهِمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ، ثم قال: وَإِنِ اسْتَنْصَرُوكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ، أثبت لهم اسم الإيمان، وجمع بينهم في الدين على تخلفهم عن الهجرة مع عظم ما فيه من الوعيد بقوله: الَّذِينَ تَوَفَّاهُمُ المَلَائِكَةُ ظَالِمِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ، وقال: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَتَّخِذُوا عَدُوِّي وَعَدُوَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَاءَ، وقال أيضا: لَا تَخُونُوا اللهَ وَالرَّسُولَ، فأثبت لهم اسم الإيمان مع قبح صنيعهم، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And also that Allah, exalted is He, preserved for him the name of faith (al-iman) while realizing what is upon him of the threat (al-wa'id) in His judgment by His statement, exalted: 'O you who have believed, why do you say what you do not do?' (61:2). So He made anger (al-maqt) necessary for him along with the name of faith, by the letter of rebuke which does not bear utterance before committing the sin by His saying: 'Why do you say?' And anger does not necessitate the sin which in wisdom requires forgiveness for him. And He said: 'And if two parties among the believers fight' (49:9), He established for them the name of faith while imposing the name of transgression (al-baghy) on one of them in the fighting, and He obligated upon those present [to make peace] until the other returns to the command of Allah. And if that were a departure from faith, the truth in such a case would be other than what He mentioned. And He said: 'O you who have believed, prescribed for you is retaliation (al-qisas) in cases of murder' (2:178), and it is known that it is not obligatory except for intentional killing. So He established for them at the beginning of the verse the name of faith, and He preserved brotherhood between them, and He informed that that is a lightening from your Lord and mercy. And these attributes are far from one whose action has removed him from faith. And He said: 'And those who believed and did not emigrate, you have no guardianship over them in anything' (8:72), then He said: 'But if they seek help from you in the religion' (8:72), He established for them the name of faith, and He brought them together in religion despite their lagging behind in emigration, along with the greatness of what is in it of the threat by His saying: 'Indeed, those whom the angels take in death while they are wronging themselves' (4:97). And He said: 'O you who have believed, do not take My enemy and your enemy as allies' (60:1), and He also said: 'Do not betray Allah and the Messenger' (8:27). So He established for them the name of faith despite the ugliness of their deed. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 931

Commentary
This passage presents a series of Qur'anic proofs demonstrating that the name 'believer' (mu'min) remains for those who commit major sins, despite the divine threat (al-wa'id) against them. Maturidi argues that Allah addresses sinners with the vocative 'O you who have believed' (يا أيها الذين آمنوا) even when rebuking them for saying what they do not do, or for fighting, or for committing intentional murder, or for not emigrating, or for taking enemies as allies, or for betraying Allah and the Messenger. In each case, the sin is grave, yet Allah still calls them 'believers' and does not remove the name of iman from them. Maturidi reasons that if these sins removed one from faith entirely, then the Qur'anic addresses would not have used the term 'believers' for them. The structure follows a pattern: each verse is cited, the sin is identified, and the continued use of 'believers' is highlighted as proof that the name remains.

Key Terms
الوعيد
اسم الإيمان
المقت
البغي
القصاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Major sins automatically remove a person from the fold of faith (iman).
Correction: The Qur'an repeatedly addresses sinners as 'believers', indicating that the name of iman remains despite major sins, as long as the person does not reject faith.

Checkpoint
Which of the following verses does Maturidi cite to show that Allah addresses sinners as 'believers' even when they commit murder?
A) يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لِمَ تَقُولُونَ مَا لَا تَفْعَلُونَ
B) يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ القِصَاصُ في القَتْلَى
C) وَإِنْ طَائِفَتَانِ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ اقْتَتَلُوا
D) يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَتَّخِذُوا عَدُوِّي وَعَدُوَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَاءَ

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an addresses sinners as 'O you who have believed,' proving that the name of iman remains despite major sins, as long as faith itself is not renounced.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you honestly feel that you are still a believer, or does your heart doubt your faith? How does this lesson challenge that doubt?
?
If Allah addresses sinners as 'believers' despite their sins, what responsibility does that place on you regarding how you view and treat fellow Muslims who struggle with sin?
?
Think of a sin you are ashamed of. Does this lesson give you hope that your iman is intact? Does it also make you more fearful of taking sin lightly? How will you respond today?

Faith and Disbelief

10 min
Quranic Proofs That Major Sinners Remain Believers
Maturidi cites multiple Quranic verses to show that faith remains despite major sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses multiple Quranic verses to prove that faith remains despite major sins, refuting the Kharijite and Mu'tazilite positions.

Core Idea
Major sins do not remove faith; the Quran consistently calls sinners 'believers'.

Maturidi was a master of Quranic reasoning. In this passage, he deploys a series of Quranic verses that all address believers who are sinning. Each verse preserves the title 'believers' for those committing major sins, showing that faith and sin can coexist. This refutes those who claim that major sins expel one from faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the overall argument. Notice the pattern: each verse addresses 'O you who have believed' followed by a prohibition or command implying sin.
This is a long passage with many proofs; read patiently.
2
Examine the first verse (61:2)
Allah rebukes the believers for saying what they do not do, yet still calls them believers. The rebuke (maqt) is not a removal of faith.
This sets the pattern: sin does not negate the name of faith.
3
Look at the fighting and retaliation verses
In Surah Al-Hujurat (49:9) and Al-Baqarah (2:178), Allah calls the parties 'believers' despite transgression and prescribes retaliation. Brotherhood among them is maintained.
If sin removed faith, such rulings would be impossible.
4
Consider the emigration and prohibition verses
In Surah Al-Anfal (8:72) and Al-Mumtahanah (60:1) and Al-Anfal (8:27), Allah addresses as believers those who failed to emigrate or are warned against betrayal, preserving the name of faith.
Even severe sins like betrayal do not remove the title of faith.
5
Reflect on the repentance verses and conclusion
Surah At-Tahrim (66:8) and An-Nur (24:31) command believers to repent, proving that they have sins that are forgiven without losing faith. Maturidi concludes that the name of faith remains.
This directly refutes those who say major sinners are no longer believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكمه بقوله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لِمَ تَقُولُونَ مَا لَا تَفْعَلُونَ، فأوجب فيه المقت عنده مع اسم الإيمان بحرف العتاب الذي لا يحتمل النطق قبل مقارفة الذنب بقوله: لِمَ تَقُولُونَ، والمقت لا يوجب الذنب الذي في الحكمة لزوم المغفرة له، وقال: وَإِنْ طَائِفَتَانِ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ اقْتَتَلُوا، أثبت لهم اسم الإيمان الزام اسم البغي لأحدهما في القتال، وألزم من حضر موته المبغى عليه حتى الآخر إلى أمر الله، ولو كان ذلك خروج من الإيمان لكان الحق في مثل ذلك غير الذي ذكر. وقال: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْقِصَاصُ فِي الْقَتْلَى، ومعلوم أنه لا يجب إلا بقتل العمد، فأثبت لهم في ابتداء الآية اسم الإيمان، وأبقى بينها الأخوة، وأخبر أن ذلك تخفيف من ربكم ورحمة، وتبعد هذه الأوصاف فيمن أخرجهم الفعل من الإيمان. وقال: وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَلَمْ يُهَاجِرُوا مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ وِلَايَتِهِمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ، ثم قال: وَإِنِ اسْتَنْصَرُوكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ، أثبت لهم اسم الإيمان، وجمع بينهم في الدين على تخلفهم عن الهجرة مع عظم ما فيه من الوعيد بقوله: الَّذِينَ تَوَفَّاهُمُ الْمَلَائِكَةُ ظَالِمِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ. وقال: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَتَّخِذُوا عَدُوِّي وَعَدُوَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَاءَ، وقال أيضا: لَا تَخُونُوا اللَّهَ وَالرَّسُولَ، فأثبت لهم اسم الإيمان مع قبح صنيعهم. وأيضا أن الله تعالى قال: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا تُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ تَوْبَةً نَصُوحًا، وقال: وَتُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ جَمِيعًا أَيُّهَا الْمُؤْمِنُونَ، أخبر أن عليهم ذنوبا تغفر بالتوبة ويكفر بها على إبقاء اسم الإيمان، وفي قول هؤلاء لا يجوز ذلك، فثبت أن القول هو قول من لم يزل عنهم اسم الإيمان، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
His ruling by His saying the Most High: 'O you who have believed, why do you say what you do not do?' So He made anger necessary for them along with the name of faith by the letter of rebuke which does not allow speech before committing the sin by His saying 'why do you say?', and anger does not necessitate the sin which in wisdom requires forgiveness for it. And He said: 'And if two groups among the believers fight', He established for them the name of faith while imposing the name of transgression on one of them in the fighting, and He required the one who witnessed his death to be the wronged one until the other comes to the command of Allah, and if that were an exit from faith, the truth in such a matter would be other than what He mentioned. And He said: 'O you who have believed, prescribed for you is legal retribution for the slain', and it is known that it is only required for intentional killing, so He established for them at the beginning of the verse the name of faith, and kept brotherhood among them, and informed that that is a lightening from your Lord and mercy, and these attributes are far from one whose action has removed him from faith. And He said: 'And those who believed and did not emigrate, for you there is no guardianship of them at all', then He said: 'But if they seek help from you in the religion', He established for them the name of faith, and brought them together in the religion despite their lagging behind in emigration with the greatness of the threat in it by His saying: 'Those whom the angels take in death while wronging themselves'. And He said: 'O you who have believed, take not My enemies and your enemies as allies', and He also said: 'Do not betray Allah and the Messenger', so He established for them the name of faith despite the ugliness of their deeds. And also that Allah the Most High said: 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with sincere repentance', and He said: 'And repent to Allah all of you, O believers', He informed that they have sins which are forgiven by repentance and expiated while preserving the name of faith, and according to the saying of these people that is not permissible. So it is established that the correct saying is the saying of those who do not remove the name of faith from them, and there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 932

Commentary
This passage is a series of Quranic proofs demonstrating that the name of faith (īmān) remains upon a believer even when he commits major sins (kabā'ir). Maturidi begins by citing Sūrat al-Ṣaff (61:2) where Allah rebukes believers for saying what they do not do, yet still addresses them as 'believers'. The rebuke implies displeasure (maqt) but not removal of faith. Then he cites Sūrat al-Ḥujurāt (49:9) about two groups of believers fighting; Allah calls them believers while condemning one group as transgressors. If sin removed faith, the ruling would be different. Next, Sūrat al-Baqarah (2:178) on retaliation: Allah addresses believers and prescribes capital punishment for intentional killing, yet still calls them believers and brothers. Then Sūrat al-Anfāl (8:72) about those who believed but did not emigrate: Allah still calls them believers despite their failure to emigrate, and Sūrat al-Nisā' (4:97) warns those who wrong themselves but still calls them believers. Then Sūrat al-Mumtaḥanah (60:1) and al-Anfāl (8:27) forbid taking enemies as allies and betraying Allah and the Messenger, yet those addressed are called believers despite the ugliness of their actions. Finally, Sūrat al-Taḥrīm (66:8) and al-Nūr (24:31) command repentance to believers, implying they have sins that are forgiven while the name of faith remains. Maturidi concludes that the correct position is that the name of faith is not removed from sinners, refuting the Kharijites and Mu'tazilites who hold that major sins expel one from faith.

Key Terms
إيمان
كبيرة
فسق
مقت
عتاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that calling a believer a 'fāsiq' (sinner) negates faith, or that major sins expel a person from faith entirely.
Correction: Maturidi shows through multiple verses that the Quran consistently calls sinners 'believers' even when rebuking them, preserving the name of faith despite major sins.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's argument from Sūrat al-Ḥujurāt (49:9), what does Allah's addressing the fighting parties as 'believers' prove?
A) That fighting removes faith.
B) That the name of faith remains despite fighting and transgression.
C) That only one party is actually a believer.
D) That the verse abrogates the obligation of brotherhood.

Key Takeaway
The name of faith is inseparable from the believer, even when committing major sins; the Quran consistently upholds this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing a major sin, do you view them as less of a believer? How does this lesson challenge your tendency to judge based on actions?
?
Have you ever felt that your own major sin has removed you from Allah’s mercy or made you a hypocrite? Based on this passage, how should you now view your relationship with Allah despite your sins?
?
Are you quick to condemn others for their shortcomings, forgetting that the Quran addresses them as 'believers' and commands you to maintain brotherhood? What concrete step will you take to treat sinning Muslims as brothers and sisters in faith?

Faith and Disbelief

Faith Persists Despite Sin: Maturidi's Argument
Maturidi argues that obligatory acts are ascribed to faith, so faith persists in the sinner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the name of faith remains with a person even if they commit major sins, based on the fact that acts of worship are obligated under the name of faith.

Core Idea
Sin does not erase faith — the obligation itself proves it remains.

Imam Maturidi presents a compelling argument from the nature of religious obligations. He notes that Allah has made many acts of worship contingent upon the name of faith. If faith were removed by sin, the sinner would no longer be obligated. Yet the sinner still participates in these acts, proving faith remains. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the original argument
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the logical flow: obligation under faith name → sinner participates → conclusion that faith remains.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the key premise
The key premise is that Allah obligated acts of worship 'under the name of faith' (bism al-īmān). This means that the obligation itself is tied to the person being a believer. If faith were lost, the obligation would be lost.
3
Draw the conclusion
Since the fāsiq (grave sinner) still participates in these acts, the name of faith is not removed. Maturidi also points to previous explanations as sufficient.
This argument is part of a larger proof that faith and sin can coexist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونوع آخر أن الله تعالى أوجب كثيرا من العبادات باسم الإيمان وجعل علم الحل والحرمة في كثير من ذلك اسم الإيمان وزواله، ثم شارك من أحدث أفعال الفسق مع الإيمان فيها غيره، ثبت أن اسم الإيمان غير زائل عنهم. مع ما قد تقدم بيان ما له اسم الإيمان ما يكفى ذا العقل عن الإطناب.
And another type: that Allah the Most High obligated many acts of worship under the name of faith, and made the knowledge of what is permissible and forbidden in much of that dependent on the name of faith and its removal. Then the one who commits acts of transgression with faith participates in them just as others do. It is established that the name of faith is not removed from them. Along with what has preceded of explanation of what belongs to the name of faith, which suffices the intelligent from verbosity.
Source pages p. 933

Commentary
This passage introduces a different type of argument. Maturidi points out that Allah has obligated various acts of worship (ʿibādāt) under the name of faith (īmān) and has made the knowledge of what is permissible (ḥalāl) and forbidden (ḥarām) in many of these acts dependent on the name of faith and its removal. If major sins removed faith, then a person committing a major sin would no longer be considered a believer and thus would not be obligated to perform these acts, nor would rulings depend on the presence or absence of faith. However, the fāsiq (grave sinner) still participates in these acts alongside other believers. Therefore, the name of faith is not removed from them. Maturidi concludes that this, combined with the previous explanations, is sufficient for any intelligent person.

Key Terms
عبادات
إيمان
فسق
حل
حرمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude from the fact that Allah obligated acts of worship under the name of faith?
A) That only sinless believers are obligated.
B) That the name of faith remains with the fāsiq.
C) That the fāsiq must repent before performing acts.
D) That acts of worship are not required from sinners.

Key Takeaway
The name of faith remains even with the fāsiq because acts of worship are obligated under that name, and the fāsiq still participates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that a sin you committed was so great that you lost your faith? How does Maturidi's argument challenge that feeling? Will you now see your sins as serious but not as faith-removing? What change in your mindset is required to embrace this truth?
?
If you are aware of a sin you commit, do you still fulfill your obligations like prayer and fasting? What does it say about your faith that you continue to do so? How can you use this argument to strengthen your resolve to worship despite your weaknesses?
?
This lesson shows that the name of faith remains even with sin. Does this comfort you or make you complacent? How will you personally avoid using this as an excuse to continue sinning? What concrete step will you take today to grow your faith rather than take it for granted?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
5 min
Proof that Faith Remains with Sinners
Maturidi argues that Quranic verses and consensus prove faith remains despite major sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses Quranic verses, obligations based on faith, and consensus to prove that major sins do not remove the name of faith.

Core Idea
Faith remains even with major sins, proven by Quran, obligation, and consensus.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi presents a multi-layered argument defending the Sunni position that believers who commit major sins retain the name of faith. He draws on Quranic commands to repent addressed to believers, the structure of religious obligations, and the unanimous practice of the Muslim community. This lesson unpacks each proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi builds his argument in three distinct stages.
2
Identify the three proofs
The passage contains three separate proofs. Find each one: the Quranic repentance verses, the obligation-based argument, and the consensus argument.
These are the three pillars of his case.
3
Understand the Quranic argument
Maturidi cites verses where Allah commands repentance and addresses sinners as 'believers.' This implies that sin does not remove the name of faith. Ask yourself: why would Allah call them believers if they had lost faith?
This refutes the Khawarij and Mu'tazila position.
4
Examine the obligation-based argument
Allah makes many acts of worship (like prayer, fasting, hajj) obligatory based on the name of faith. Sinners who still perform these acts share in the reward, proving faith remains.
5
Reflect on the consensus argument
The Muslim community has always prayed for forgiveness and mercy for all who die facing the qibla, and affirmed intercession for sinners. This consensus is a decisive proof.
This shows the position is upheld by the entire ummah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن الله تعالى قال: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا تُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ تَوْبَةً نَصُوحًا، وقال: وَتُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ جَمِيعًا أَيُّهَا الْمُؤْمِنُونَ، أخبر أن عليهم ذنوبا تغفر بالتوبة ويكفر بها على إبقاء اسم الإيمان، وفي قول هؤلاء لا يجوز ذلك، فثبت أن القول هو قول من لم يزل عنهم اسم الإيمان، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ونوع آخر أن الله تعالى أوجب كثيرا من العبادات باسم الإيمان وجعل علم الحل والحرمة في كثير من ذلك اسم الإيمان وزواله، ثم شارك من أحدث أفعال الفسق مع الإيمان فيها غيره، ثبت أن اسم الإيمان غير زائل عنهم. مع ما قد تقدم بيان ما له اسم الإيمان ما يكفي ذا العقل عن الإطناب. ثم إجماع النقلة في إثبات الشفاعة، وتوارث الأمة في الصلاة على جميع من مات القبلة والاستغفار لهم والترحم عليهم هو الدليل لمن أبت نفسه تكذيب الأخبار الصحاح ومخالفة أئمة الهدى، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Also that Allah Most High said: 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with sincere repentance,' and said: 'And repent to Allah, all of you, O believers.' He informed that upon them are sins that are forgiven by repentance and expiated while preserving the name of faith. And according to the saying of these [opponents], that is not permissible. So it is established that the correct saying is the saying of those from whom the name of faith has not departed. And there is no power except with Allah. And another type: Allah Most High made obligatory many acts of worship under the name of faith, and made the knowledge of the lawful and unlawful in much of that [dependent on] the name of faith and its removal. Then He shared [the reward] with others who commit acts of transgression along with faith. So it is established that the name of faith does not depart from them. Along with what has preceded of explanation concerning what the name of faith entails, which suffices the intelligent from prolixity. Then the consensus of the transmitters in affirming intercession, and the succession of the community in prayer over all who die facing the qibla, and seeking forgiveness for them, and invoking mercy upon them, is the evidence for one whose soul refuses to belie the authentic traditions and oppose the imams of guidance. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 933

Commentary
This passage presents a multi-layered proof that the name of faith (iman) remains with believers who commit major sins. The author first cites two Quranic verses (Quran 66:8 and 24:31) where Allah addresses sinners as 'believers' and commands repentance, implying that sin does not nullify faith. The opponents (Khawarij and Mu'tazila) hold that such people lose the name of faith, but this verse contradicts their view. Second, the author notes that Allah makes many obligations contingent on the name of faith itself (e.g., pilgrimage, jihad), and shares rewards with those who commit sins alongside faith, proving faith remains. Third, he points to the consensus of the transmitters (naqala) on affirming intercession (shafa'a) for sinners, and the continuous practice of the Muslim community praying for forgiveness and mercy over all who die facing the qibla, regardless of their sins. This consensus is a decisive proof against those who reject authentic reports and oppose the guided imams. The passage concludes with 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' as a humble acknowledgment of divine aid.

Key Terms
إيمان
توبة
إجماع
شفاعة
قبلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that committing a major sin removes the name of faith entirely, making the person a disbeliever.
Correction: Maturidi shows that Quranic verses, the structure of religious obligations, and community consensus all affirm that the name of faith remains with sinners, who are still called believers and are eligible for repentance, reward, and intercession.

Checkpoint

B) Verses commanding repentance while addressing believers
C) Verses about the punishment of disbelievers

Key Takeaway
The name of faith remains with sinful believers, as proven by Quranic address, obligation structure, and community consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight with a major sin you haven't repented from, do you truly believe you would still be counted among the believers? Why or why not? Let this question drive you to seek repentance now, not despair.
?
The passage shows that Allah addresses sinners as 'believers' when commanding repentance. Does your daily attitude toward your own sins reflect a confidence that you are still a believer, or do you secretly suspect that your sins have removed you from the fold? What would change if you truly believed the name of faith remains?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing a major sin, do your thoughts align with the teaching that their faith remains, or do you find yourself doubting their faith? What does that reveal about your understanding of the mercy of Allah? Ask Allah to give you a heart that hopes for them as it hopes for yourself.

Major Sins are of Two Types: Belief and Action
Maturidi classifies major sins into two types and clarifies avoidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's classification of major sins into sins of belief and sins of action, and how this refutes the Mu'tazila interpretation of Quran 4:31.

Core Idea
Major sins are not all alike; sins of belief and sins of action are treated differently.

Maturidi begins his refutation of the Mu'tazila by examining the verse 'If you avoid the major sins...' He points out that the verse does not specify the ruling for those who do not avoid, and then establishes a critical distinction: major sins are of two fundamentally different types. This distinction is key to understanding how divine forgiveness operates.

Guided Path
1
Contextualize the debate
Recognize that Maturidi is countering the Mu'tazila and Khawarij interpretation that the verse implies all major sins must be avoided for forgiveness.
2
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the logical flow: verse citation, absence of ruling, classification, and conclusion.
Pay attention to the terms 'كبائر في الاعتقاد' and 'كبائر الأفعال'.
3
Identify the two types
Maturidi states that major sins are of two types: those in belief (like kufr and shirk) and those in actions. Note that sins of belief are the ones that differentiate disbelievers.
The phrase 'التي بها اختلفت الكفرة' indicates belief sins are the root of disbelief.
4
Understand the nuance of avoidance
Maturidi explains that a person who commits a major action sin while acknowledging its gravity is still considered 'avoiding' in one sense, but committing it is a contravention. The verse does not address those who fail to avoid.
This shows that the verse's primary referent is avoidance of belief sins.
5
Consider the implications for forgiveness
Maturidi concludes that the praised avoidance is specifically of belief sins (shirk), and Allah forgives other sins for whom He wills, by good deeds or grace.
This refutes the Mu'tazila claim that the verse implies all major sins must be avoided to avoid punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم للآية وجوه تمنع قول المعتزلة والخوارج أحدها أنه قال : إِن تَجْتَنِبُوا كَبَائِرَ مَا تُنْهَوْنَ عَنْهُ ، وليس في ذلك بيان حكم من لا يجتنب . ثبت أن الكبائر نوعان : أحدهما كبائر في الاعتقاد من أنواع الكفر والتكذيب التي بها اختلفت الكفرة ، وأخرى كبائر الأفعال التي صاحبها مجتنب عنها بالانتفاء في أن يراها على ما جعلها الله عليه من عظم الفعل والذنب ، وهذا اجتناب ، وقد وقعها بالفعل، فهو الارتكاب ، وليس في الآية وجه الاجتناب ، فجائز أن يُحمد : أن يجتنب كبائر الاعتقاد ، وهي أنواع الشرك فيكفر عنها دونها لمن يشاء . ذلك من الحسنات أو بالتفضل كما بينا في إحدى الآيتين بالتحف وفي الأخرى بالمغفرة ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then for the verse there are aspects preventing the saying of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij, one of which is that He said: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden from' — and there is not in that a statement of the ruling for one who does not avoid. It is established that major sins are of two types: one of them is major sins in belief, from the types of disbelief and denial by which the disbelievers differed; and another is major sins of actions, the doer of which is one who avoids them by way of [؟] in considering them as Allah has made them, of the gravity of the action and sin — and this is avoidance — yet he commits them by action, so that is commission. And there is not in the verse a face of avoidance. So it is possible that it is praised: that one avoids major sins of belief, and they are types of shirk, and He forgives besides them for whom He wills. That is from good deeds or by grace, as we explained in one of the two verses with the gift and in the other with forgiveness. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 937

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification passage. Maturidi presents the first of several aspects that refute the Mu'tazila and Khawarij interpretation of Quran 4:31 ('If you avoid the major sins...'). He points out that the verse does not specify the ruling for one who does not avoid major sins. Then he establishes that major sins are of two types: first, sins of belief (i'tiqad), which include the various types of disbelief (kufr) and denial (takdhib) that distinguish different groups of disbelievers; second, sins of action (af'al). He explains that a person who commits a major action sin while recognizing its gravity is still in a state of avoidance in one sense (since he acknowledges its sinfulness), but actually committing it is a contravention. The verse does not address anyone who fails to avoid. Maturidi then suggests that the praised avoidance may refer specifically to avoiding sins of belief (i.e., shirk), and Allah forgives other than shirk for whomever He wills, either through good deeds or by His grace, as explained elsewhere.

Key Terms
كبائر (major sins)
اعتقاد (belief)
كفر (disbelief)
تكذيب (denial)
الشرك (shirk)
الاجتناب (avoidance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse implies that avoiding all major sins is necessary for forgiveness and that those who commit any major sin are doomed.
Correction: Maturidi shows the verse does not specify the fate of non-avoiders, and that major sins are of two types; avoidance of belief sins is the primary condition for forgiveness.

Checkpoint

A) Sins of belief and sins of action
B) Sins of the tongue and sins of the limbs
C) Sins against God and sins against people
D) Sins that require repentance and sins that do not

Key Takeaway
Maturidi divides major sins into sins of belief (shirk) and sins of action, arguing that avoidance of belief sins is what merits forgiveness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you distinguish between sins of belief (like doubts about Allah’s mercy) and sins of action? How does Maturidi’s classification force you to evaluate which type you truly fear?
?
If the forgiveness promised in the verse is primarily for avoiding sins of belief like shirk, does that make you less concerned about your major sins of action? What is your heart’s real stance on shirk compared to other sins?
?
Maturidi says that even when you commit a major sin of action, you can be 'avoiding' it in one sense. Is your repentance a genuine rejection of the sin itself, or just regret? Examine your own avoidance: do you truly see the sin as Allah sees it—a grave offense?

The Invalidity of Inferring Lying from Apostasy
Maturidi refutes the inference from apostasy to lying in initial belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi considers the inference from later apostasy to prove initial belief was a lie to be invalid and the absurd consequences that follow.

Core Idea
Later actions cannot negate the sincerity of initial belief.

Maturidi begins his refutation of a dangerous argument: if someone later apostatizes, does that prove their initial faith was a lie? He declares this inference invalid and shows how it leads to contradictions regarding the rulings of apostates and original disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp Maturidi's initial argument.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
Notice that the opponent infers from refraining (later apostasy) that the first belief was a lie.
This is the view being refuted.
3
Follow the absurd consequences
Maturidi shows that if this inference held, it would erase the distinction between apostates and original disbelievers, and would also imply that a disbeliever's later faith proves his first disbelief was a lie.
These are reductio ad absurdum arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستدلال من استدل بترك الفعل على الكذب فى الأول محال فاسد؛ لأن في عقل كل واحد لزوم اتقاء الكذب كما في القبول إبقاؤه، ثم لم يصر وجوده دليلا على كذب عقله، لما في عقله منعه، وإن تعدى ذلك فمثله في قبول وقت تعديه، ولو كان فى ذلك تبين لكان كل شيء بالأول، أو خل يجب فساده وحرمته، ولو كان كذلك لكان لا يجب على المرتد خلاف على الكافر الأصلى بل بتصريح الكفر لا يظهر كذبه فى الأول، فكيف فيما فعل ؟ ولو كان بذا ذا فيظهر أيضا بإيمان الكافر من بعد أو بتعاطيه ما لا يقبحه على كذبه في العرف . وأصله وجهان : أحدهما لو كان يظهر به الكذب في الاول لأزيل اللزوم ، وإذا زال ليبطل أن يصير وجوده سببا لإظهار ذلك ، وفيه بطلان ما قالوا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . والثاني إن كلاً يعلم من نفسه في وقت اعتقاده أنه غير كاذب في ذلك ، ثم يعلم من تعدى فى دينه ، ولو كان به ظهور لكان لا علم يقع في الحقيقة ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ، بل مدعى هذا يلزمه ذلك؛ إذ في اعتقاده أن لا يكذب ، وكل مؤمن يعلم أنه بهذا القول كاذب ، وكذلك الله سبحانه؛ إذ هو يعلم حقيقة كل شيء بما هو عليه لا بغيره يعلم صدقه فى الأول . وإن تعدى من بعده فيصير صاحب هذا القول عند الله وعند من شهد عليه بالكذب كاذبا ، فيستوجب به من كل أحد القضاء عليه بالكفر فى قوله الذى يريد به تثبیت کفر غيره ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وقوله تعالى : إِنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا ثُمَّ آمَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا ولو كان في ذلك ما ذكر لم يكن ليثبت لهم إيمان أبدا ، فثبت به فساد قولهم. فهذا في الكفر ، فكيف فيما دونه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى ذلك اختلاف الأحوال في الخلق لا يو حب فساد مضاداتها في غير تلك الأحوال ، وبالله التوفيق .
And the inference of one who infers from refraining from action upon lying in the first [belief] is invalid and corrupt. Because in the intellect of every person there is an obligation to avoid lying just as in acceptance there is its preservation. Then its existence did not become evidence for the lie of his intellect, because in his intellect there is prevention of it. And if it transcends that, then its like is in acceptance at the time of its transgression. And if in that there were clarification, then everything would be by the first, or it would necessitate its corruption and prohibition. And if it were so, then there would be no obligation upon the apostate different from the original disbeliever; rather, by explicit disbelief his lie in the first [belief] does not appear, so how about what he did? And if it were this, it would also appear by the disbeliever's subsequent faith or by his undertaking what does not make him ugly due to his lying in custom. And its basis is two aspects: First, if lying in the first were to appear through it, then the obligation would be removed. And if it is removed, it would become invalid that its existence becomes a cause for showing that. And in this is the invalidity of what they said, and there is no power except with Allah. Second, everyone knows from himself at the time of his belief that he is not lying in that. Then he knows about one who transgresses in his religion. And if it were to appear through it, then no knowledge would occur in reality, and there is no power except with Allah. Rather, the claimant of this is bound by that; because in his belief he does not lie, and every believer knows that he is by this statement a liar. Likewise Allah, exalted; for He knows the reality of everything as it is, not by something else does He know his truthfulness in the first. And if one after him transgresses, then the holder of this statement becomes in the sight of Allah and in the sight of one who testifies against him as a liar, so he becomes deserving from everyone of the judgment of disbelief upon him in his statement by which he intends to establish the disbelief of others, and there is no power except with Allah. And the saying of the Exalted: 'Indeed, those who believed then disbelieved then believed then disbelieved' (4:137). And if in that were what they mentioned, then faith would never be established for them. So the corruption of their saying is established. This is regarding disbelief, so how about what is less than it? And there is no power except with Allah. And accordingly, the differing of states in creation does not necessitate the corruption of their opposites in other than those states. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 938

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an argument made by opponents. The argument is: one who initially believes but then commits an act of disbelief (like apostasy) shows by his later action that his initial belief was a lie. Maturidi refutes this as invalid and corrupt. He begins by stating why: every person's intellect obligates avoiding lying, and this obligation is preserved even when one accepts belief. The existence of later disbelief does not prove that the intellect's initial belief was a lie, because the intellect itself prevents lying. If one argues that later action transcends the initial belief, then the same logic would apply to acceptance itself at the time of transgression—leading to absurd consequences. For example, if this reasoning were valid, then everything would be judged by the first act, which would corrupt the obligation of apostasy rulings distinguishing apostates from original disbelievers. Moreover, if later action indicated lying in the first belief, then a disbeliever's subsequent faith would also indicate that his first disbelief was a lie—which is absurd. Maturidi then presents two fundamental aspects (wajhan) of the refutation:

First, if later action revealed lying in the first belief, then the obligation (luzūm) to avoid lying would be removed. Once the obligation is removed, the existence of the action cannot be a cause for revealing the lie. This invalidates the opponent's claim.

Second, every person knows from himself at the time of his belief that he is not lying in that belief. Then he also knows about one who later transgresses in his religion. If later action were to reveal lying, then no certain knowledge would be possible in reality—because everyone's self-knowledge of sincerity would be undermined. The claimant of this argument is himself bound by it: he believes in his own belief that he does not lie, but every believer knows that the claimant is by this statement a liar. Likewise, Allah knows the truth of everything as it is, not by external signs, and He knows the sincerity of the original belief. If someone later apostasies, then the claimant's statement would make him a liar in Allah's sight and before witnesses, deserving the judgment of disbelief upon himself—since his statement aims to establish the disbelief of others, but instead establishes his own.

Finally, Maturidi cites the Quranic verse 'Indeed, those who believed then disbelieved then believed then disbelieved' (4:137). If the opponent's claim were true, such people could never have faith established for them after repeated disbelief. But the verse acknowledges their faith after disbelief, showing the corruption of the opponent's argument. Maturidi concludes: if this argument fails regarding disbelief, how much more so for lesser sins? And the differing states in creation do not necessitate the corruption of their opposites in other states. This comprehensive refutation upholds the sincerity of initial belief despite later apostasy.

Key Terms
استدلال
ترك الفعل
الكذب
الأول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Apostasy proves that the initial faith was insincere or a lie.
Correction: Maturidi shows this leads to logical absurdities and contradicts self-knowledge of sincerity.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say would happen if the inference from refraining to lying were valid?
A) Apostates would be treated the same as original disbelievers
B) A disbeliever's later faith would prove his first disbelief was a lie
C) Both A and B
D) It would confirm the truth of initial belief

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the argument that later apostasy proves initial belief was a lie by showing it leads to absurd theological and logical consequences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted the sincerity of someone's faith because they later committed a major sin or abandoned religion? How does Maturidi's argument challenge you to reconsider that judgment, and what would it look like to take this lesson to heart today?
?
Think of a time when you felt your own past acts of worship or declarations of faith were rendered meaningless by a later failure. How does this lesson call you to view your own journey—not as a series of cancelations, but as a record of sincerity that only Allah knows?
?
If you knew that a disbeliever might later embrace Islam, would you consider their initial disbelief a lie? Why or why not? Now apply that same logic to yourself: are you willing to extend the same grace to others that you hope for yourself?

The Two Fundamental Refutations of the Inference
Maturidi presents two wajhan (aspects) to refute the inference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two core arguments Maturidi presents to definitively refute the claim that later actions reveal lying in initial belief.

Core Idea
Self-knowledge of sincerity and the condition of obligation refute the inference.

Maturidi presents two fundamental aspects (wajhan) that expose the logical flaws in the opponent's argument. The first deals with the removal of obligation, and the second with the impossibility of certain knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the two aspects
Carefully read each wajh (aspect) and notice how they target different premises of the opponent.
2
First aspect: obligation removed
If later action revealed lying, the obligation to avoid lying would be lifted, undermining the cause.
Without obligation, the action cannot be a sign.
3
Second aspect: self-knowledge
Every person knows they are not lying at the moment of belief; if later action revealed lying, no knowledge would be possible.
Also applies to Allah's knowledge.
4
See the implication for the claimant
The one making this claim himself believes he is not lying, but his statement makes him a liar.
He becomes deserving of the judgment of disbelief.

واستدلال من استدل بترك الفعل على الكذب فى الأول محال فاسد؛ لأن في عقل كل واحد لزوم اتقاء الكذب كما في القبول إبقاؤه، ثم لم يصر وجوده دليلا على كذب عقله، لما في عقله منعه، وإن تعدى ذلك فمثله في قبول وقت تعديه، ولو كان فى ذلك تبين لكان كل شيء بالأول، أو خل يجب فساده وحرمته، ولو كان كذلك لكان لا يجب على المرتد خلاف على الكافر الأصلى بل بتصريح الكفر لا يظهر كذبه فى الأول، فكيف فيما فعل ؟ ولو كان بذا ذا فيظهر أيضا بإيمان الكافر من بعد أو بتعاطيه ما لا يقبحه على كذبه في العرف . وأصله وجهان : أحدهما لو كان يظهر به الكذب في الاول لأزيل اللزوم ، وإذا زال ليبطل أن يصير وجوده سببا لإظهار ذلك ، وفيه بطلان ما قالوا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . والثاني إن كلاً يعلم من نفسه في وقت اعتقاده أنه غير كاذب في ذلك ، ثم يعلم من تعدى فى دينه ، ولو كان به ظهور لكان لا علم يقع في الحقيقة ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ، بل مدعى هذا يلزمه ذلك؛ إذ في اعتقاده أن لا يكذب ، وكل مؤمن يعلم أنه بهذا القول كاذب ، وكذلك الله سبحانه؛ إذ هو يعلم حقيقة كل شيء بما هو عليه لا بغيره يعلم صدقه فى الأول . وإن تعدى من بعده فيصير صاحب هذا القول عند الله وعند من شهد عليه بالكذب كاذبا ، فيستوجب به من كل أحد القضاء عليه بالكفر فى قوله الذى يريد به تثبیت کفر غيره ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وقوله تعالى : إِنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا ثُمَّ آمَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا ولو كان في ذلك ما ذكر لم يكن ليثبت لهم إيمان أبدا ، فثبت به فساد قولهم. فهذا في الكفر ، فكيف فيما دونه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى ذلك اختلاف الأحوال في الخلق لا يو حب فساد مضاداتها في غير تلك الأحوال ، وبالله التوفيق .
And the inference of one who infers from refraining from action upon lying in the first [belief] is invalid and corrupt. Because in the intellect of every person there is an obligation to avoid lying just as in acceptance there is its preservation. Then its existence did not become evidence for the lie of his intellect, because in his intellect there is prevention of it. And if it transcends that, then its like is in acceptance at the time of its transgression. And if in that there were clarification, then everything would be by the first, or it would necessitate its corruption and prohibition. And if it were so, then there would be no obligation upon the apostate different from the original disbeliever; rather, by explicit disbelief his lie in the first [belief] does not appear, so how about what he did? And if it were this, it would also appear by the disbeliever's subsequent faith or by his undertaking what does not make him ugly due to his lying in custom. And its basis is two aspects: First, if lying in the first were to appear through it, then the obligation would be removed. And if it is removed, it would become invalid that its existence becomes a cause for showing that. And in this is the invalidity of what they said, and there is no power except with Allah. Second, everyone knows from himself at the time of his belief that he is not lying in that. Then he knows about one who transgresses in his religion. And if it were to appear through it, then no knowledge would occur in reality, and there is no power except with Allah. Rather, the claimant of this is bound by that; because in his belief he does not lie, and every believer knows that he is by this statement a liar. Likewise Allah, exalted; for He knows the reality of everything as it is, not by something else does He know his truthfulness in the first. And if one after him transgresses, then the holder of this statement becomes in the sight of Allah and in the sight of one who testifies against him as a liar, so he becomes deserving from everyone of the judgment of disbelief upon him in his statement by which he intends to establish the disbelief of others, and there is no power except with Allah. And the saying of the Exalted: 'Indeed, those who believed then disbelieved then believed then disbelieved' (4:137). And if in that were what they mentioned, then faith would never be established for them. So the corruption of their saying is established. This is regarding disbelief, so how about what is less than it? And there is no power except with Allah. And accordingly, the differing of states in creation does not necessitate the corruption of their opposites in other than those states. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 938

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an argument made by opponents. The argument is: one who initially believes but then commits an act of disbelief (like apostasy) shows by his later action that his initial belief was a lie. Maturidi refutes this as invalid and corrupt. He begins by stating why: every person's intellect obligates avoiding lying, and this obligation is preserved even when one accepts belief. The existence of later disbelief does not prove that the intellect's initial belief was a lie, because the intellect itself prevents lying. If one argues that later action transcends the initial belief, then the same logic would apply to acceptance itself at the time of transgression—leading to absurd consequences. For example, if this reasoning were valid, then everything would be judged by the first act, which would corrupt the obligation of apostasy rulings distinguishing apostates from original disbelievers. Moreover, if later action indicated lying in the first belief, then a disbeliever's subsequent faith would also indicate that his first disbelief was a lie—which is absurd. Maturidi then presents two fundamental aspects (wajhan) of the refutation:

First, if later action revealed lying in the first belief, then the obligation (luzūm) to avoid lying would be removed. Once the obligation is removed, the existence of the action cannot be a cause for revealing the lie. This invalidates the opponent's claim.

Second, every person knows from himself at the time of his belief that he is not lying in that belief. Then he also knows about one who later transgresses in his religion. If later action were to reveal lying, then no certain knowledge would be possible in reality—because everyone's self-knowledge of sincerity would be undermined. The claimant of this argument is himself bound by it: he believes in his own belief that he does not lie, but every believer knows that the claimant is by this statement a liar. Likewise, Allah knows the truth of everything as it is, not by external signs, and He knows the sincerity of the original belief. If someone later apostasies, then the claimant's statement would make him a liar in Allah's sight and before witnesses, deserving the judgment of disbelief upon himself—since his statement aims to establish the disbelief of others, but instead establishes his own.

Finally, Maturidi cites the Quranic verse 'Indeed, those who believed then disbelieved then believed then disbelieved' (4:137). If the opponent's claim were true, such people could never have faith established for them after repeated disbelief. But the verse acknowledges their faith after disbelief, showing the corruption of the opponent's argument. Maturidi concludes: if this argument fails regarding disbelief, how much more so for lesser sins? And the differing states in creation do not necessitate the corruption of their opposites in other states. This comprehensive refutation upholds the sincerity of initial belief despite later apostasy.

Key Terms
وجهان
لزوم
علم
اعتقاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: External actions can reveal the inner truth of past beliefs.
Correction: Maturidi shows this would remove the obligation and destroy certain knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's first aspect, what would happen if later action revealed lying?
A) The obligation to avoid lying would be removed
B) The obligation would be strengthened
C) The action would become a cause for truth
D) Self-knowledge would be confirmed

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's two aspects refute the inference by showing it destroys the obligation to avoid lying and undermines self-knowledge of sincerity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted the sincerity of your own faith because of a later sin or a period of doubt? How does Maturidi's argument about self-knowledge at the time of belief challenge that doubt?
?
Do you hold others to a standard of consistency between their initial declarations and later actions, even when you wouldn't want that standard applied to yourself? Reflect on the trap Maturidi identifies in the claimant's logic.
?
When you face accusations about the purity of your intentions, do you trust your own inner knowledge or are you swayed by external judgments? Maturidi says everyone knows their own sincerity. Can you act on that knowledge with confidence?

The Quranic Evidence and Final Conclusion
Maturidi uses Quranic evidence and a final principle to conclude his refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quran 4:137 and a final general principle to conclusively refute the argument that apostasy proves initial insincerity.

Core Idea
The Quranic case of repeated belief and disbelief disproves the inference.

Maturidi seals his refutation with a powerful Quranic verse that describes people who believed, then disbelieved, then believed, then disbelieved. If the opponent's inference held, such people would never have had true faith. He then concludes with a general principle about states and their opposites.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse
Recite the verse and note its implication: it describes multiple changes of belief.
Surah An-Nisa (4:137).
2
Apply the opponent's logic
If their inference were true, then after the first disbelief, the second faith would be impossible because the first disbelief would have been a lie. Maturidi says: if the inference held, faith would never be established for them.
3
Understand the conclusion
The corruption of the opponent's saying is established. The argument fails for disbelief, so even more so for lesser sins.
4
Grasp the final principle
Differing states in creation do not necessitate the corruption of their opposites in other states.
This is a general logical principle.

Refutation of the Claim that Lying Is Evident
Imam Maturidi refutes the claim that lying is evident from actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Maturidi argues that lying is not evident from a person's actions and how this refutes certain theological claims.

Core Idea
Lying cannot be externally evident; if it were, knowledge and judgment would be impossible.

Imam Maturidi challenges the claim that lying can be known from a person's outward actions. He shows that if lying were evident, it would lead to logical absurdities, such as the inability to distinguish between an apostate and an original disbeliever, and the impossibility of certain knowledge. This passage lays out two key arguments against the evident nature of lying.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow before you interpret.
Notice that the passage uses 'one' and 'the second' to introduce two arguments.
2
Identify the two aspects (wajhān)
The passage presents two arguments against the claim. Find where each begins and note how they are structured.
3
Analyze the first aspect
Consider the first argument: if lying were apparent, the necessary link between action and judgment would be removed, leading to invalidity.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Analyze the second aspect
The second argument: everyone knows their own truthfulness, so if lying were evident, no one could have certain knowledge of another's inner state.
This appeals to self-awareness and divine knowledge.
5
Reflect on the Qur'anic verse
Maturidi quotes verse 4:137 about those who believe, disbelieve, then believe again. If lying were evident, such alternation would be impossible, proving the claim false.
This is a practical illustration of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعديه، ولو كان في ذلك تبين لكان كل شيء بالأول، أو خل يجب فساده وحرمته، ولو كان كذلك لكان لا يجب على المرتد خلاف على الكافر الأصلي بل بتصريح الكفر لا يظهر كذبه في الأول، فكيف فيما فعل؟ ولو كان بذا [؟] ذا فيظهر أيضا بإيمان الكافر من بعد أو بتعاطيه ما لا يقبحه على كذبه في العرف. وأصله وجهان: أحدهما لو كان يظهر به الكذب في الأول لأزيل اللزوم، وإذا زال ليبطل أن يصير وجوده سببا لإظهار ذلك، وفيه بطلان ما قالوا، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والثاني إن كلا يعلم من نفسه في وقت اعتقاده أنه غير كاذب في ذلك، ثم يعلم من تعدى في دينه، ولو كان به ظهور لكان لا علم يقع في الحقيقة، ولا قوة إلا بالله، بل مدعي هذا يلزمه ذلك؛ إذ في اعتقاده أن لا يكذب، وكل مؤمن يعلم أنه بهذا القول كاذب، وكذلك الله سبحانه؛ إذ هو يعلم حقيقة كل شيء بما هو عليه لا بغيره يعلم صدقه في الأول. وإن تعدى من بعده فيصير صاحب هذا القول عند الله وعند من شهد عليه بالكذب كاذبا، فيستوجب به من كل أحد القضاء عليه بالكفر في قوله الذي يريد به تثبيت كفر غيره، ولا قوة إلا بالله، وقوله تعالى: "إِنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا ثُمَّ آمَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا"، ولو كان في ذلك ما ذكر لم يكن ليثبت لهم إيمان أبدا، فثبت به فساد قولهم. فهذا في الكفر، فكيف فيما دونه، ولا قوة إلا بالله
His transgression, and if it were apparent in that, then everything would be by the first, or [something] whose corruption and prohibition are necessary. And if it were like that, then it would not be obligatory upon the apostate differently from the original disbeliever, but by declaring disbelief his lie does not appear in the first [state], so how about what he did? And if it were by this [unclear] then it would also appear by the belief of the disbeliever afterwards or by his undertaking what does not deem him a liar in custom. Its basis has two aspects: one: if lying were apparent by it in the first [state], then the necessity would be removed, and when it is removed, it would render his existence a cause for showing that invalid, and in it is the invalidity of what they said, and there is no power except with Allah. The second: that everyone knows from himself at the time of his conviction that he is not lying in that, then he knows the one who transgressed in his religion, and if there were appearance by it, then no knowledge would occur in reality, and there is no power except with Allah. Rather, the claimant of this is bound by that, because in his conviction he does not lie, and every believer knows that he is lying by this statement, and likewise Allah Almighty, for He knows the reality of everything as it is, not by another does He know his truthfulness in the first. And if the one after him transgresses, then the holder of this statement becomes at the time of Allah and those who testify against him as a liar, so he deserves by it from everyone the judgment of disbelief upon him in his statement by which he intends to establish the disbelief of others, and there is no power except with Allah. His statement Almighty: "Indeed, those who have believed then disbelieved, then believed then disbelieved..." and if there were in that what was mentioned, their faith would never be established. So the corruption of their statement is established. This is regarding disbelief, so how about what is less than it? And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 939

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a claim that lying (kadhb) is evident from a person's actions or statements, so that it could serve as a basis for judgments about faith and disbelief. The author, Imam Maturidi, argues against this claim by showing its logical consequences. He begins by stating that if lying were apparent, then it would lead to absurdities such as not distinguishing between an apostate and an original disbeliever. He then presents two aspects (wajhān) of the argument. The first is that if lying were evident, the necessary link between an action and its judgment would be removed, invalidating the claim. The second is that every person knows in his own conviction that he is not lying, and if lying were evident, no one could have certain knowledge of another's truthfulness. The author further argues that the claimant of this view is himself bound by it, because he believes he is not lying, yet others consider him a liar. Allah knows the truth of all things. The passage concludes with a Qur'anic verse (4:137) about those who alternate between faith and disbelief, implying that if lying were evident, such alternation would be impossible, thus proving the error of the claim.

ظهور
كفر

Checkpoint
According to Imam Maturidi, what would be the consequence if lying were evident from a person's actions?
A) No one could be certain of another's truthfulness.
B) Apostasy would be impossible.
C) All believers would be considered disbelievers.
D) The disbeliever's faith would be accepted.

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi demonstrates that if lying were evident, it would lead to contradictions, such as the removal of necessary judgments and the impossibility of certain knowledge, thus proving the claim false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time you felt certain someone was lying or hypocritical based on their actions. How does this lesson challenge that certainty? Can you honestly say you knew their inner state? How will you judge differently now?
?
If outward actions cannot definitively prove inner faith, what does that mean for how you view fellow Muslims who commit sins? Are you quick to label them as having weak faith? What would it take for you to reserve judgment?
?
The passage says every believer knows from himself that he is not lying at the time of conviction. Reflect: Are you fully honest with yourself about your own sincerity? When you perform acts of worship, do you ever doubt your own intention? Commit to checking your heart before judging others.

The Inconsistency of Mu'tazila on Major Sins
Maturidi exposes a logical flaw in Mu'tazila theology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical inconsistency in the Mu'tazila position on major sins regarding the naming of major sinners as 'people of prayer and qibla'.

Core Idea
If faith is the basis for the name, then when sin removes faith, the name should also cease.

Imam Maturidi begins his refutation by pointing out a contradiction in the Mu'tazila stance. They affirm that perpetrators of major sins are still called 'people of prayer and qibla' because they have faith, yet they also hold that major sins remove that same faith. Maturidi argues that this is logically inconsistent: the basis for the name vanishes, so the name should vanish with it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse every word. Let the author's argument sink in before interpreting.
The passage contains an unclear word 'تحال' but the overall meaning is clear.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila claim
Find where Maturidi describes what the Mu'tazila affirm about major sinners and why.
They affirm the name 'people of prayer and qibla' based on faith.
3
Understand Maturidi's objection
Maturidi argues that if faith is the cause, and faith is removed by sin, the name should be removed. This is a logical contradiction.
The text says 'that by which it is established has ceased'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا أيضا يلزم المعتزلة في الكبائر، ثم العجب من هؤلاء يثبتون لأصحاب الكبائر اسم أهل الصلاة [و] القبلة، وسبب إثبات هذا الاسم لهم الإيمان، تحال [؟] زواله على بقاء ذلك، وما به ثبت قد زال، والله أعلم. وقوله: وقد روي في الآية القراءة على أن تجتنبوا كبير ما تتهون عنه، وإن كان المعروف ذلك فإنه قد يجوز إرادة الآحاد بحرف الجمع، فلا ننكر أن تكون الآية على ذلك، يبين ذلك قوله تعالى: "وَمَنْ يُكْفِيرُ [؟] بِالإِيمَانِ" و] َ مَن يَتْبَعْ غَيْرَ الإِسْلامِ دِينًا[، وقوله: "وَمَنْ يَرْتَدِدْ مِنْكُمْ عَنْ دِينِهِ"، وعلى ذلك تأويل قوله: "إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ"، ثم قال: "وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ"، كما قال في هذا: "وَيُكَفِّرْ عَنْكُمْ سَيِّئَاتِكُمْ" فيكون الإتيان بحكم واحد، ومعلوم أن لا ترك للمعتزلة والخوارج في أحدهما، فكذلك في الأخرى. ثم الأصل أن قوله: "إِنْ تَجْتَنِبُوا كَبَائِرَ مَا تُنْهَوْنَ عَنْهُ نُكَفِّرْ عَنْكُمْ سَيِّئَاتِكُمْ"، على قول الخوارج كأنه قال: إن تجتنبوا الكفر والشرك، وعلى قول المعتزلة: إن تجتنبوا الخروج من الإيمان نكفر عنكم ما ذكر، فلا كبيرة إذن على قولهم إلا الخروج من الإيمان، فصارت الآية على قولهم راجعة إلى خاص، وهو ما يخرج عن الدين والإيمان، فأبطل ذلك قولهم في دعوى العموم فيها، وألزم القول بالخصوص، فمن قضى شيء دون شيء بلا بيان فهو متحكم، وفي ذلك لزوم قول الحسين من الوقف في جميع ما فيه الوعيد وبطلان قول من ذكر، والله أعلم
And this also applies to the Mu'tazila regarding major sins. Then the wonder from these [people] is that they affirm for the perpetrators of major sins the name of 'people of prayer and qibla', and the reason for affirming this name for them is faith, [but] the removal [of faith] [unclear] upon the permanence of that, and that by which it is established has ceased. And Allah knows best. And His statement: And it has been narrated in the verse the reading that you avoid the major [sins] of what you are prohibited from, and if that is well-known, then it may be intended as singular by the plural particle, so we do not deny that the verse is upon that. That is shown by His statement: 'And whoever disbelieves in faith' [and whoever follows a religion other than Islam], and His statement: 'And whoever among you apostatizes from his religion', and upon that is the interpretation of His statement: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him', then He said: 'And He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills', as He said in this: 'And He will expiate for you your evil deeds', so the coming of a single ruling is [implied]. And it is known that there is no escape for the Mu'tazila and Khawarij from one of them, so likewise in the other. Then the principle: His statement: 'If you avoid the major [sins] of what you are prohibited from, We will expiate for you your evil deeds', according to the saying of the Khawarij is as if He said: If you avoid disbelief and polytheism, and according to the saying of the Mu'tazila: If you avoid exiting from faith, We will expiate for you what is mentioned, so there is no major sin then according to their saying except exiting from faith. Thus the verse according to their saying returns to the specific, which is what exits from religion and faith. So that invalidates their claim of generality in it, and necessitates the saying of specificity. For whoever judges something without [specifying] something else without explanation is an arbitrary ruler. And in that is the necessary implication of the saying of Husayn [al-Najjar?] of stopping (waqf) in all that contains threat, and the invalidity of the saying of those mentioned. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 940

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij positions regarding major sins (kaba'ir). The author points out the inconsistency of the Mu'tazila, who affirm that perpetrators of major sins are still called 'people of prayer and qibla' based on their faith, yet they hold that such people are in a state between faith and disbelief. The author argues that if faith is the cause of that name, then when sin removes faith in the afterlife (according to them), the name should also cease. Then he discusses the interpretation of the Qur'anic verse (4:31) about avoiding major sins. He notes that the verse could be interpreted in a singular sense despite the plural phrasing, citing other verses about specific sins like shirk, apostasy, and disbelief. He argues that the Mu'tazila and Khawarij are committed to contradictory positions: the Khawarij say major sins are only kufr and shirk, while the Mu'tazila say they are only 'exiting faith'. Thus, the verse would be specific, not general, to these categories, invalidating their claim of generality. He concludes by stating that this leads to the position of stopping (waqf) on all threats, as held by al-Husayn (al-Najjar), and refutes those who claim otherwise.

Key Terms
كبائر
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mu'tazila consistently hold that major sinners have diminished faith but still belong to the community.
Correction: Maturidi shows that their own logic implies that if faith is the basis for the name, then removing faith (as they claim sin does) must remove the name.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the basis for the Mu'tazila calling major sinners 'people of prayer and qibla'?
A) Their prayers
B) Their faith
C) Their repentance
D) Their Islamic identity

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila position on major sins is internally inconsistent because the basis for naming someone 'people of prayer and qibla' is faith, which they claim sin removes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider your own life: Do you ever claim the name 'Muslim' or 'believer' based on your faith, yet act in ways that contradict that faith? What specific inconsistency will you work to remove this week?
?
The Mu'tazila are criticized for saying the name depends on faith but denying faith remains after sin. In your heart, do you ever feel that after a major sin, you are still 'the same believer'? How does this passage challenge you to be honest about the state of your faith?
?
If faith is the basis for your identity as a Muslim, and a sin can weaken or even remove that faith, how seriously do you take protecting your iman? Write one concrete step you will take today to strengthen it.

The Qur'anic Verse and the Refutation of Generality
Maturidi analyzes Quran 4:31 to refute sectarian interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses the interpretation of Quran 4:31 to refute both the Mu'tazila and Khawarij, and how this leads to the position of waqf on threat verses.

Core Idea
By restricting major sins to kufr or exiting faith, both sects make the verse specific, not general, invalidating their claims.

Imam Maturidi now turns to the Qur'anic verse about avoiding major sins to receive expiation. He notes that the verse can be interpreted as referring to a single major sin, like kufr or shirk. He cites other verses where Allah specifies that He does not forgive shirk but forgives lesser sins. The Khawarij and Mu'tazila each interpret the major sins in the verse as exclusive to kufr or exiting faith respectively, thereby limiting the verse's application. Maturidi argues that this renders their claim of generality invalid and necessitates the position of waqf — suspending judgment on all threat verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Note the frequent quotation of other verses.
The passage contains variant readings and several scriptural citations.
2
Identify the key verse and its interpretation
The verse in question is 'If you avoid the major sins...' Maturidi mentions a variant reading that suggests a singular meaning.
3
Note the supporting verses
Maturidi cites verses about shirk, apostasy, and disbelief to show that forgiveness is specific for less than shirk.
These verses show a pattern of specificity.
4
Analyze the implications for Mu'tazila and Khawarij
Both groups interpret the verse as exclusively referring to kufr (Khawarij) or exiting faith (Mu'tazila). This makes the verse specific to those categories, not general.
Thus their claim of generality is refuted.
5
Understand the conclusion: waqf
Maturidi concludes that the only consistent position is to suspend judgment (waqf) on all threat verses, as held by al-Husayn al-Najjar.
This refutes the Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

?

Are you willing to let the Qur'an correct you, even when it hurts?
?

Was that judgment based on your own standards or on divine criteria? How can you train yourself to pause and seek Allah's guidance before making such judgments?
?

This lesson shows that true submission means being willing to have your assumptions dismantled by the truth. Would you be able to accept being wrong if the Qur'an and Sunnah proved it? What would that cost you?
