Refutation of claim that abandoning minor sins is faith
Maturidi refutes the claim that abandoning minor sins is faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that abandoning minor sins equals faith leads to a logical contradiction.

Core Idea
Claiming that avoiding sins is faith leads to absurd consequences.

Maturidi now turns to refute a specific claim: that the act of leaving minor sins counts as faith. This claim seems plausible but leads to a logical trap. The passage exposes this by showing what follows if the claim is taken seriously.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then its translation. Notice the opponent's claim and the author's response.
The opponent argues that abandoning minor sins is faith because punishment follows if one does not avoid them.
2
Identify the author's objection
The author refutes by drawing a consequence: If abandoning minor sins is faith, then committing major sins must also be faith. This is absurd.
The author uses the opponent's own logic against them.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The author calls the position 'extreme confusion.' Consider why this label fits.
The claim leads to self-contradiction, showing it cannot be true.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم زعم أن ترك الصغائر إيمان؛ لما يعاقب عليها لو لم يجتنب الكبائر. فيقال له: إذا يجب أن يكون إيمانا عند ارتكاب الكبائر، ولما يعذب على ضد ذلك، وليس بإيمان إذا اجتنب، وذلك غاية الحيرة.
Then he claimed that leaving minor sins is faith, because one is punished for them if one does not avoid major sins. So it is said to him: Then it must be faith when committing major sins, and because one is punished for the opposite of that, and it is not faith if one avoids them, and that is extreme confusion.
Source pages p. 946

Commentary
This passage refutes a specific claim that abandoning minor sins constitutes faith. The author points out the logical inconsistency: if leaving minor sins is faith because one is punished for not avoiding them, then it would also follow that committing major sins is faith, and avoiding them would not be faith. This leads to absurdity, showing the claim is flawed.

الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That leaving minor sins is inherently an act of faith
Correction: The author shows this leads to absurdity; faith is not defined by avoiding sins alone.

Checkpoint

A) It contradicts the Quran
B) It would make committing major sins also faith
C) It is not based on any proof
D) It ignores the role of repentance

Key Takeaway
The claim that abandoning minor sins is faith collapses because it leads to the opposite conclusions.

Refutation on Seeking Forgiveness for the Wicked
Maturidi refutes the argument against seeking forgiveness for the wicked by clarifying definitions and presenting two criticisms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the argument that seeking forgiveness for the wicked is impermissible, and the two key criticisms he raises.

Core Idea
The meaning of 'wicked' determines the ruling; Maturidi exposes confusion in the opposition's argument.

Maturidi now addresses an objection: some claim that seeking forgiveness for a 'wicked' person is not permissible. He first demands a clear definition of 'wicked', then presents two powerful criticisms. This passage sharpens our understanding of how terms matter in theological debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the English translation. Get a feel for the flow of argument.
Notice the opponent's claim is stated briefly at the start.
2
Identify the opponent's claim and Maturidi's clarification
Look for the sentence where Maturidi asks what 'wicked' means. Understand the two possible meanings and their implications.
This clarification is key to the refutation.
3
Study the first criticism about the label 'wicked'
Maturidi argues that applying the label 'wicked' when no wicked act is occurring is problematic. Faith can be present simultaneously.
This criticism relies on the relationship between name and action.
4
Study the second criticism about prophets' forgiveness
Maturidi argues that the opponent's interpretation of prophets seeking forgiveness implies ingratitude and is impossible.
5
Reflect on the overall refutation
Consider how the two criticisms work together to refute the absolute prohibition. How does this affect your understanding of seeking forgiveness?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج بها بما لا يجوز عند الأمة الاستغفار للفاجر. فيقال له: ما يعنى بالفاجر الكافر أو الذي يرتكب كبيرة في حال إيمان بلا استحلال؟ فإن قال الأول حاد عن الاعتدال، وإن قال بالثاني كذب على الأمة وجعله دليلا لاستحقاقه الخلود في النار بما ظهر من صنيعه فمبذول له ما تمنى في نفسه. ثم عليه فيه أمران: أحدهما إطلاق الاسم بالفجور مرة وهو في حالة فيه ولا فعل فجور يجوز اطلاق الاسم بالإيمان وهو فيه ومعه حقيقة فعله بالسمع والعقل بل لا يجوز إطلاق اسم الفجور حتى يبين، وجائز ذلك في الإيمان بما جاء به القرآن واتفق عليه أهل اللسان، ولا قوة إلا بالله جميعا، والثاني أنه صرف استغفار الأنبياء والأولياء إلى ما هو مغفور، وذلك كتمان نعمة الغفران وإعراض عن الشكر فيها ذلك حقه، وذلك بعيد ممتنع، والله الموفق.
Then he argued with it that it is not permissible according to the community to seek forgiveness for the wicked. So it is said to him: What does he mean by 'wicked'? Is it the disbeliever or the one who commits a major sin while in a state of faith without deeming it lawful? If he says the first, he deviates from moderation. If he says the second, he lies about the community and makes it a proof for his deserving eternal punishment by what appears from his action, so what he wished for himself is granted to him. Then there are two matters against him in it: First, applying the name of wickedness when he is in a state in which there is no act of wickedness; it is permissible to apply the name of faith while he is in it and with him is the reality of his action by hearing and reason, but it is not permissible to apply the name of wickedness until it is clarified; and that is permissible in faith by what the Quran brought and the people of language agreed upon, and there is no power except with Allah. Second, that he turns the seeking of forgiveness of the prophets and saints to what is forgiven, and that is concealing the blessing of forgiveness and turning away from gratitude for it, which is its due, and that is far and impossible, and Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 946

Commentary
This passage addresses an argument about not seeking forgiveness for the wicked (الفاجر). The author objects by asking for clarification of the term. If it means disbeliever, the opponent deviates from the middle way; if it means a sinful believer, the opponent lies about the consensus. The author then presents two criticisms: (1) the opponent applies the label of wickedness at a time when no act of wickedness is occurring, whereas faith can be applied simultaneously, and this is consistent with the Quran and language; (2) the opponent misinterprets the seeking of forgiveness by prophets and saints, implying ingratitude. Thus the argument is refuted.

الاستغفار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: That the prohibition on seeking forgiveness for a 'wicked' person is absolute regardless of definition.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the ruling depends on the meaning of 'wicked'; the opponent's position is incoherent because they do not specify.

Checkpoint

A) The label is never appropriate
B) The opponent applies it when no wicked act is present
C) The opponent does not define the term

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the blanket prohibition of seeking forgiveness for the wicked by clarifying the term and showing logical flaws in the opponent's position.

The Dilemma of Specification in the Verse on Consuming Wealth
Imam Maturidi critiques specification and poses a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Maturidi's critique of the specification of the verse on consuming wealth and the logical dilemma he presents to those who argue that sin removes faith.

Core Idea
The verse on consuming wealth does not negate faith; it is specified, and removing it leads to a contradiction.

Imam Maturidi continues his refutation by examining the verse about consuming wealth unjustly (Quran 4:29). He shows that opponents agree on specification, yet fail to apply the same logic to the mention of faith in the verse. This passage presents a powerful dilemma that forces the opponent into a corner.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Let the author's own reasoning come through before you analyze it.
Notice the parallel with the earlier discussion on killing.
2
Understand the two points about specification
The passage makes two points: first, the verse is specified to taking a little, not large amounts; second, it mentions transgression and wrongdoing, which may refer to worldly punishment, not removal of faith.
This shows that the verse does not imply the sinner is no longer a believer.
3
Grasp the dilemma
The key dilemma: the verse addresses believers ('O you who have believed'). The author asks opponents: do you remove that address or keep it? Both options lead to consequences they would not accept.
If they remove it, they admit specification without evidence; if they keep it, they agree the person remains a believer.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The opponent is forced to either admit specification (which undermines their position) or accept that the sinner is still a believer, which aligns with the Murji'a view they oppose.
This refutes the idea that major sins negate faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكر من أكل المال بالباطل فكل يجمع على التخصيص ؛ إذ ذلك اسم بأخذ القليل ، وذلك غير مراد فيه ، وكذلك أموال اليتامى . والثاني أنه ذكر فيه عدوانا وظلما ، وذلك على العذاب على حد الله والظلم على صاحبه ، مع احتمال ذلك ما ذكرنا في القتل . ثم يقال لهم : الآية التي فيها ذكر الإيمان أتزيله أو تبقيه ؟ فإن أزاله فقد أقر بالتخصيص ، وإن أبقاه رجع إلى رأى من نسبهم إلى الإرجاء ، والله الموفق .
And what is mentioned about consuming wealth unjustly — all of it is agreed upon specification; because that is a name for taking a little, and that is not intended in it, and likewise the wealth of orphans. The second is that it mentions transgression and wrongdoing, and that is about punishment in this world and wrongdoing upon its perpetrator, while it is possible that it is what we mentioned about killing. Then it is said to them: The verse in which faith is mentioned — do you remove it or keep it? If he removes it, he has admitted specification, and if he keeps it, he returns to the opinion of those who attribute them to irja' (postponement), and Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 949

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the refutation, now turning to the verse about consuming wealth unjustly (Quran 4:29). The author argues that opponents agree that this verse is specified (takhsis) — that is, it does not apply to all cases. For example, it may refer only to taking small amounts, or it may refer to punishment in this world, similar to the earlier discussion on killing. The key point is the dilemma: the verse contains the phrase 'O you who have believed' (ya ayyuha alladhina amanu), which addresses believers. The author asks: do you remove that address (i.e., claim it does not mean they are believers) or keep it? If you remove it, you admit to specification without evidence. If you keep it, you effectively agree that the person remains a believer despite the sin, which is the position of the Murji'a (those who postpone judgment). This forces the opponent into a logical corner.

Key Terms
أكل المال بالباطل
تخصيص
إرجاء
إيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse on consuming wealth unjustly removes faith from the believer, meaning the sinner is no longer a believer.
Correction: The verse is specified and does not remove faith; the address 'O you who have believed' remains, indicating the sinner is still considered a believer in the Quranic address.

Checkpoint
What dilemma does Imam Maturidi pose to opponents regarding the verse that addresses believers concerning consuming wealth?
A) They must either accept that the verse abrogates previous rulings or reject it.
B) They must either remove the address to believers (admitting specification) or keep it (agreeing the person is still a believer).
C) They must choose between literal and metaphorical interpretation.
D) They must decide whether the punishment is in this world or the next.

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi uses the dilemma of removing or keeping the address to believers to show that specification does not negate faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the phrase 'O you who have believed' in the verse about consuming wealth unjustly, what does it mean for how you view a believer who falls into that sin? Do you remove the address from them in your heart, or keep it? How does that affect your treatment of them?
?
Imam Maturidi shows that removing the address leads to an unjustified specification. In your own life, have you ever removed the label of 'believer' from someone based on a sin, without considering the full context of the Quranic address? What would it take to restore that label?
?
The author presents a dilemma with no easy escape. Is there any area of your faith where you hold a position that collapses under similar logical scrutiny? Would you rather admit the inconsistency or change your view? Be honest.

The Contradiction of Denying the Name of Faith
Imam Maturidi refutes the opponent's initial claim and explains the metaphorical usage of 'iman'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi exposes the self-contradiction in the opponent's argument that knowledge does not constitute belief.

Core Idea
To deny the name while affirming its linguistic basis is self-contradictory.

Imam Maturidi begins by addressing a claim that mere knowledge of the Prophet does not make one a believer. He immediately identifies a logical flaw: the opponent admits that the language applies the name 'faith' to such knowledge, yet he forbids it. This contradiction forms the core of the first refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Imam Maturidi uses a very direct and critical tone.
2
Identify the opponent's claim and Maturidi's response
The opponent claims that knowing the Prophet's truthfulness does not make one a believer, and that the linguistic application of 'iman' is not based on language. Maturidi responds by pointing out a contradiction: the opponent affirms the linguistic meaning but then forbids it.
Look for the phrase 'دل أن إطلاق الاسم ليس على ما كان في اللغة'.
3
Understand the metaphorical nature of knowledge as faith
Maturidi clarifies that knowledge (ma'rifa) is not iman in reality, but it is called iman metaphorically as a bounty from Allah that calls to belief. This is an important nuance.
The author says 'سما المعرفة ليست بإيمان، وإن سميت مجازا'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : ان الذي قال امتحن رسول الله لأعرف أنه رسول الله فأرد عليه بعد المعرفة فعرف صدقه إنه لا يكون بتلك المعرفة مؤمنا ، دل أن إطلاق الاسم ليس على ما كان في اللغة قال الفقيه رحمه الله : فنقول وبالله التوفيق : ما أعظم جهله إذا أثبت الام في اللغة كأنه قال : أطلقته اللغة وأنا أمنعه ، فهو إذا يكذب نفسه عند ذلك ما فيه ايجاب أن الله قد منعهم عن العمل بما عرفهم وألزمهم العمل مع بما جهاهم ذلك ، ذلك ، جل الله عن هذا الوصف سما المعرفة ليست بإيمان ، وإن سميت مجازا يسمى فضل الله ورحمته بما تدعو إلى التصديق ، وما ذكر كله خيال لا معنى له ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ثم استدل على منع اسم الإيمان بما جعل الله لما أطلق له اسم الإيمان أحكاما منعت منه ، واسم الكفر أحكاما لمن يقرن به . فيقال له : ما الدليل على أن الذي أوصيت إليه من الأحكام لإطلاق دون معان تتصل به في الوجهين جميعا ؟ ثم قال : منها التعظيم والتزكية والموالاة وقبول الشهادة. فيقال : ما الدلالة على أن كل هذا لإطلاق الإسم خاصة دون تحقيقه بالشرائط المضمومة إليه والعادات التي دعا إليها الإيمان ؟ وبعد ، فان ولاية الإيمان لازمة ، وجميع ما منع منه منع بحق الإيمان الذى
He said: The one who said that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) tested (someone) to know that he is the Messenger of Allah, so he rejected him after knowing (that), then he knew his truthfulness — that he does not become a believer by that knowledge — indicates that the application of the name is not (based) on what was in the language. The faqih (Imam Maturidi), may Allah have mercy on him, said: We say, and with Allah is success: How great is his ignorance when he affirmed the (name of faith) in the language? It is as if he said: The language applied it but I forbid it. So he thus contradicts himself. This includes that Allah has prevented them from acting upon what He made known to them and made obligatory upon them to act together with what they were ignorant of. Allah is exalted above this description. Knowledge is not faith, even if it is called metaphorically the bounty of Allah and His mercy that calls to belief. All that he mentioned is imagination with no meaning, and there is no power except with Allah. Then he argued to prevent the name of faith by (saying) that Allah has made for what He called by the name of faith rulings that prevent (some things), and the name of disbelief (has) rulings for those who are associated with it. It is said to him: What is the evidence that the rulings you referred to are for the application (of the name) alone without the meanings attached to it in both cases? Then he said: Among them are glorification, purification, loyalty, and acceptance of testimony. It is said: What is the evidence that all of this is for the application of the name specifically without its realization by the conditions attached to it and the customs that faith calls to? Moreover, the guardianship of faith is necessary, and everything that is prevented from is prevented by the right of faith which...
Source pages p. 949

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an opponent who argued that knowing the Prophet's truthfulness does not make one a believer, and therefore the linguistic application of the name 'iman' (faith) does not correspond to its actual usage. The author, Imam Maturidi, begins by pointing out a self-contradiction: the opponent admits the language applies the name, but then forbids it. This is inconsistent. He then clarifies that knowledge (ma'rifa) is not itself iman, though it may be called iman metaphorically as a bounty from Allah that leads to belief. The second part addresses an additional argument: the opponent claims that because the name 'iman' brings with it certain rulings (like honor, purification, loyalty, acceptance of testimony), those rulings are merely due to the name. The author counters by asking: what proof is there that these rulings are attached to the mere name rather than to the reality of iman realized through its conditions and practices? Finally, he asserts that the guardianship (wilaya) of iman is binding, and all prohibitions associated with iman are due to the true right of iman, not just the label.

Key Terms
معرفة
إيمان
لغة
إطلاق الاسم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That knowledge of the Prophet is identical to faith, or that it has no relationship to faith.
Correction: Knowledge is not iman, but it is a bounty from Allah that calls to belief, and the language applies the name metaphorically.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Maturidi refute the opponent's claim that the linguistic application of 'iman' is not based on language?
A) He cites a consensus among linguists.
B) He shows the opponent contradicts himself by affirming the linguistic meaning while denying its application.
C) He argues that language is irrelevant to theology.
D) He provides a new definition of iman.

Key Takeaway
The opponent's argument is self-contradictory because he affirms the linguistic usage but denies its application.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself affirming something with your tongue but denying it in your actions? How does the opponent's contradiction mirror your own inconsistencies in living out your faith?
?
The opponent denied the name of faith to someone who had knowledge. Are there areas in your life where you have clear knowledge of truth but resist letting it become faith that moves your heart?
?
Knowledge is a bounty that calls to belief. Have you treated knowledge of Allah as a mere fact rather than a personal call to respond? What is one step you can take today to let your knowledge lead you to deeper iman?

Refuting the Argument from Rulings
Imam Maturidi refutes the opponent's argument that the rulings of faith are attached to the name alone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the claim that the rulings associated with faith are due to the name alone.

Core Idea
Rulings are attached to the reality of faith, not just the name.

The opponent further argues that because the name 'faith' carries certain rulings (like honor and purification), these rulings are merely due to the label. Imam Maturidi challenges this by asking for evidence that the rulings are for the name alone, not for the actual realization of faith through its conditions and practices.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: the opponent presents an argument, and Maturidi responds with a question.
The passage ends abruptly; we only have Maturidi's initial counter-question.
2
Identify the opponent's argument and Maturidi's counter
The opponent argues that because the name 'iman' brings rulings like glorification, purification, loyalty, and acceptance of testimony, these rulings are due to the name alone. Maturidi asks: what evidence is there that these rulings are for the mere name without the attached conditions and practices?
Look for the phrase 'فيقال له: ما الدليل على أن الذي أوصيت إليه من الأحكام لإطلاق دون معان تتصل به'.
3
Reflect on the implication
Maturidi's question implies that rulings are not merely nominal but are based on the reality of faith achieved through its conditions. He further asserts that the guardianship (wilaya) of iman is necessary and all prohibitions are by the right of faith.
The last sentence is incomplete but reinforces that prohibitions are due to the true right of iman.

Faith and Disbelief

Are Rulings Attached to the Name or the Reality of Faith?
Objection and rebuttal about rulings attached to the name of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that rulings attached to 'iman' should prevent the name from being used for sinners, and Al-Maturidi's demand for evidence that these rulings are for the mere name rather than the reality of faith.

Core Idea
Rulings follow the reality of faith, not just the name.

Al-Maturidi engages with an opponent who argues that the very existence of rulings such as veneration and alliance for the name of faith proves that the name is not applied to sinners. In this passage, the author challenges the opponent to provide evidence that those rulings are attached to the mere name without consideration of the conditions and practices that constitute true faith. This sets the stage for understanding that the rulings derive from the reality of faith within a person.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note how the opponent lists specific rulings that supposedly prevent the name of faith, and then note the author's rebuttal asking for proof that these rulings are for the name alone.
The opponent's list includes veneration, purification, alliance, and acceptance of testimony.
2
Identify the key question
The author asks: what evidence is there that the rulings are for the mere name (الإطلاق) without the meanings (معان) and conditions (شرائط) of faith? This is the central challenge.
This question forces the opponent to consider that rulings might be based on the reality of faith.
3
Reflect on the underlying principle
Consider why Al-Maturidi insists on this distinction. It preserves the possibility that a person can have faith yet still be subject to penalties, because the rulings are not about the name but about the faith itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم استدل على منع اسم الإيمان بما جعل الله لما أطلق له اسم الإيمان أحكاما منعت منه، واسم الكفر أحكاما لمن يقرن به. فيقال له : ما الدليل على أن الذي أوصيت إليه من الأحكام لإطلاق دون معان تتصل به في الوجهين جميعا؟ ثم قال : منها التعظيم والتزكية والموالاة وقبول الشهادة. فيقال : ما الدلالة على أن كل هذا لإطلاق الإسم خاصة دون تحقيقه بالشرائط المضمومة إليه والعادات التي دعا إليها الإيمان؟ وبعد، فان ولاية الإيمان لازمة، وجميع ما منع منه منع بحق الإيمان الذي فيه؛ إذ حقيقته فيه منعنا عما ذكر، ما كان الثابت مما فيه الحدود والقصاص ولم يكن له الولاية ويجب له الشهادة، وجميع ما ذكر وتقبل ويحد على ذلك، لأحد نفى الإسم بما [؟] عفى عن عذاب الله، بل ذلك كله كما قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: عصموا منى دماءهم وأموالهم إلا بحقها، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيد ذلك قوله: "ولا تأخذكم بهما رأفة في دين الله"، إنه لو كان الإيمان زائلا عنه لكانت الرأفة لا تأخذه، بل رأفة الإيمان هي التي تأخذه حتى لعلها تبلغ إلى تعطيل الحد، فحدد ذلك وأيد ذلك ما لو تاب، ولا قوة إلا بالله وإقامة الحد من الرحمة لأنه يكفره ويزيل عنه. والأصل أن عقوبات الكفر لا تظهر صاحبها بل تسلمه إلى عذاب الأبد كقوله: "أغرقوا فأدخلوا نارا"، والحدود والقصاص جعلت كفارات، فثبت أنها جعلت كذلك، لم يزل الإيمان عنه، والله أعلم
Then he argued to prevent the name of faith by what God has made for whom He has allowed the name of faith—rulings that prevent him from it, and the name of disbelief has rulings for those who are associated with it. So it is said to him: What is the evidence that the rulings you have assigned are for the mere name without meanings attached to it in both cases? Then he said: Among them are veneration, purification, alliance, and acceptance of testimony. So it is said: What is the indication that all of this is specifically for the mere name without its realization through the conditions attached to it and the practices that faith calls to? Moreover, indeed the alliance of faith is necessary, and all that is prevented from him is prevented by the right of faith which is in him; since its reality in him prevents us from what was mentioned. Whatever is established among the capital punishments and retaliations, and he does not have alliance but testimony is obligatory for him, and all that was mentioned is accepted and he is punished for that, no one denies the name because of what is forgiven of God's punishment. Rather, all of that is as he said, peace be upon him: 'They protect from me their blood and their wealth except by their right.' And there is no power except with God. And this is supported by His statement: 'Let not pity for them seize you in the religion of God.' If faith were removed from him, pity would not seize him. Rather, the pity of faith is what seizes him, such that it may almost reach suspending the punishment. So He specified that, and it is supported by his repentance. And there is no power except with God. And the establishment of the punishment is from mercy because it expiates him and removes it from him. And the principle is that the punishments of disbelief do not purify its owner but deliver him to eternal punishment, as His statement: 'Drown them and cause them to enter a fire.' And the capital punishments and retaliations were made expiations. So it is established that they were made thus, faith is not removed from him. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 949

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The opponent argues that the name 'iman' is prevented because God attached to it specific rulings (like veneration, alliance, acceptance of testimony) that would not apply if the name were not present. The response (in the voice of the author) asks: what is the proof that those rulings are for the mere name rather than for the meaning and conditions of faith? The opponent then lists some of those rulings. The reply counters: those rulings are actually due to the reality of faith (the true faith within the person). The passage then discusses that capital punishments and other penalties do not negate the name of faith; rather, they are expiations. The Prophet's hadith about protecting blood and wealth is cited, and the Quranic verse about not showing pity in executing punishments is used to show that executing the punishment is a mercy because it expiates the sin and preserves the faith. The origin is that punishments of disbelief lead to eternal punishment, while capital punishments and retaliations are expiations, proving that faith remains with the person despite the punishment.

Key Terms

أحكام
التعظيم
التزكية
الموالاة
الشهادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the mere name 'iman' automatically brings rulings, so a sinner cannot be called a believer.
Correction: Rulings are attached to the reality of faith, not the name alone, so a sinner with faith retains the name.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the opponent's initial argument regarding the name of faith?
A) That the name of faith is prevented because God attached rulings that would prevent it.
B) That the name of faith is preserved regardless of rulings.
C) That rulings are attached only to the reality of faith.
D) That the opponent has no argument.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi insists that rulings attached to faith are based on its reality, not the mere name, so the name can still be applied to believers who commit sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call yourself a believer, do you examine whether the practices and conditions of faith are present in your life, or do you rely on the label alone? How would your daily life change if you truly believed that veneration, purification, alliance, and acceptance of testimony are attached to the reality of your faith, not just the name?
?
Al-Maturidi challenges the opponent to provide evidence that rulings are for the mere name. What evidence can you provide from your own life that your faith is not just a name but a reality with conditions? Will you hold yourself accountable today for the actions that faith demands?
?
The opponent thought the name alone should grant privileges. Do you ever expect respect or recognition from others simply because you are Muslim, without examining the state of your heart? What would it mean for you to pursue the reality of faith this week, even if it costs you the name?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate

The Expiatory Punishments Do Not Negate Faith
Proof that capital punishments are expiations and do not remove faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that capital punishments and retaliations are expiations (kafarat) that do not remove the name of faith, and that they are acts of mercy that purify the believer.

Core Idea
Punishments expiate sins and preserve faith, not negate it.

After establishing that rulings are attached to the reality of faith, Al-Maturidi addresses a potential concern: if a Muslim commits a crime that warrants capital punishment, does that not mean the person has lost faith? He argues that such punishments are expiations (kafarat) and acts of mercy, citing the Prophet's hadith about protecting blood and wealth, and the Quranic verse against showing pity in executing punishments. This lesson explores the evidence that punishments do not negate faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on punishments
Read the Arabic text from 'وبعد' to the end. Notice how Al-Maturidi discusses alliance (ولاية), capital punishments (حدود), and retaliations (قصاص).
The passage includes a hadith and a Quranic verse.
2
Understand the argument about alliance
Al-Maturidi states that the alliance of faith is necessary, and that punishments are imposed by right of faith. This means the person still has faith, otherwise the punishment would be for disbelief.
The phrase 'بحق الإيمان الذي فيه' is key.
3
Examine the hadith and verse
The hadith 'They protect from me their blood and their wealth except by their right' indicates that believers retain protection unless a just punishment applies. The verse 'Let not pity for them seize you in the religion of God' shows that executing punishment is a religious duty, and the lack of pity is not due to absence of faith but to uphold justice.
4
Grasp the expiatory nature
Al-Maturidi explains that the hadd and qisas are made expiations (kafarat). They purify the believer, whereas punishments of disbelief lead to eternal punishment. Therefore, imposing such punishments actually confirms that the person is a believer undergoing purification.
Contrast with the verse about drowning Pharaoh's people.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم استدل على منع اسم الإيمان بما جعل الله لما أطلق له اسم الإيمان أحكاما منعت منه، واسم الكفر أحكاما لمن يقرن به. فيقال له : ما الدليل على أن الذي أوصيت إليه من الأحكام لإطلاق دون معان تتصل به في الوجهين جميعا؟ ثم قال : منها التعظيم والتزكية والموالاة وقبول الشهادة. فيقال : ما الدلالة على أن كل هذا لإطلاق الإسم خاصة دون تحقيقه بالشرائط المضمومة إليه والعادات التي دعا إليها الإيمان؟ وبعد، فان ولاية الإيمان لازمة، وجميع ما منع منه منع بحق الإيمان الذي فيه؛ إذ حقيقته فيه منعنا عما ذكر، ما كان الثابت مما فيه الحدود والقصاص ولم يكن له الولاية ويجب له الشهادة، وجميع ما ذكر وتقبل ويحد على ذلك، لأحد نفى الإسم بما [؟] عفى عن عذاب الله، بل ذلك كله كما قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: عصموا منى دماءهم وأموالهم إلا بحقها، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيد ذلك قوله: "ولا تأخذكم بهما رأفة في دين الله"، إنه لو كان الإيمان زائلا عنه لكانت الرأفة لا تأخذه، بل رأفة الإيمان هي التي تأخذه حتى لعلها تبلغ إلى تعطيل الحد، فحدد ذلك وأيد ذلك ما لو تاب، ولا قوة إلا بالله وإقامة الحد من الرحمة لأنه يكفره ويزيل عنه. والأصل أن عقوبات الكفر لا تظهر صاحبها بل تسلمه إلى عذاب الأبد كقوله: "أغرقوا فأدخلوا نارا"، والحدود والقصاص جعلت كفارات، فثبت أنها جعلت كذلك، لم يزل الإيمان عنه، والله أعلم
Then he argued to prevent the name of faith by what God has made for whom He has allowed the name of faith—rulings that prevent him from it, and the name of disbelief has rulings for those who are associated with it. So it is said to him: What is the evidence that the rulings you have assigned are for the mere name without meanings attached to it in both cases? Then he said: Among them are veneration, purification, alliance, and acceptance of testimony. So it is said: What is the indication that all of this is specifically for the mere name without its realization through the conditions attached to it and the practices that faith calls to? Moreover, indeed the alliance of faith is necessary, and all that is prevented from him is prevented by the right of faith which is in him; since its reality in him prevents us from what was mentioned. Whatever is established among the capital punishments and retaliations, and he does not have alliance but testimony is obligatory for him, and all that was mentioned is accepted and he is punished for that, no one denies the name because of what is forgiven of God's punishment. Rather, all of that is as he said, peace be upon him: 'They protect from me their blood and their wealth except by their right.' And there is no power except with God. And this is supported by His statement: 'Let not pity for them seize you in the religion of God.' If faith were removed from him, pity would not seize him. Rather, the pity of faith is what seizes him, such that it may almost reach suspending the punishment. So He specified that, and it is supported by his repentance. And there is no power except with God. And the establishment of the punishment is from mercy because it expiates him and removes it from him. And the principle is that the punishments of disbelief do not purify its owner but deliver him to eternal punishment, as His statement: 'Drown them and cause them to enter a fire.' And the capital punishments and retaliations were made expiations. So it is established that they were made thus, faith is not removed from him. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 949

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The opponent argues that the name 'iman' is prevented because God attached to it specific rulings (like veneration, alliance, acceptance of testimony) that would not apply if the name were not present. The response (in the voice of the author) asks: what is the proof that those rulings are for the mere name rather than for the meaning and conditions of faith? The opponent then lists some of those rulings. The reply counters: those rulings are actually due to the reality of faith (the true faith within the person). The passage then discusses that capital punishments and other penalties do not negate the name of faith; rather, they are expiations. The Prophet's hadith about protecting blood and wealth is cited, and the Quranic verse about not showing pity in executing punishments is used to show that executing the punishment is a mercy because it expiates the sin and preserves the faith. The origin is that punishments of disbelief lead to eternal punishment, while capital punishments and retaliations are expiations, proving that faith remains with the person despite the punishment.

Key Terms
الموالاة
الحدود
القصاص
الكفارات
الرأفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That capital punishment (hadd) removes a person from the fold of faith.
Correction: Hadd is an expiation that purifies the believer, and faith remains; the punishment is from mercy.

Checkpoint
What is the main function of capital punishments (hadd) and retaliations (qisas) according to Al-Maturidi in this passage?
A) They prove that the person has lost faith.
B) They are punishments that lead to eternal torment.
C) They are expiations (kafarat) and acts of mercy.
D) They are meant to show pity on the offender.

Key Takeaway
Capital punishments and retaliations are expiations that do not remove faith; they are acts of mercy that purify the believer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a sin you have committed that you were never caught for. If you had been punished for it in this world, would you have seen that punishment as a mercy from God? How does this lesson challenge your desire to hide your faults rather than seek purification?
?
When you see someone being punished for a crime, what is your immediate emotional response? Does your pity ever lead you to question whether the punishment is too harsh? How does Al-Maturidi's reasoning about pity and faith reshape how you should view such punishments?
?
This lesson says that faith remains despite major sins. Is there any sin you have committed that makes you feel as though your faith is lost? How can you hold onto the truth that the very fact you are held accountable is a sign of your faith, and that seeking repentance and accepting consequences are acts of mercy from God?

Refuting an Intermediate Category Between Faith and Disbelief
Al-Maturidi refutes the concept of an intermediate status between faith and disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Maturidi insists on a binary division between faith and disbelief and how he refutes the notion of an intermediate category.

Core Idea
There is no middle ground between faith and disbelief in Islam's theological framework.

This passage comes from Imam al-Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid, where he responds to an opponent who posits a third category between faith and disbelief. Al-Maturidi argues that God's division of humanity is strictly binary—believers and disbelievers—and any claim of an intermediate is an innovation unsupported by scripture.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that al-Maturidi uses a very direct and argumentative style.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent argues that God's rulings are divided into three categories: faith, disbelief, and what is between them. This sets up the need for an intermediate (wasit).
The opponent's premise is rejected by al-Maturidi.
3
Understand al-Maturidi's binary response
Al-Maturidi asserts that God divides humans into two categories in all matters. Adding a third is innovation (bid‘a).
This is the core of his refutation.
4
Analyze the hadith and innovation charge
The hadith condemns sheltering an innovator, and al-Maturidi applies it to the one who invents a third category.
The hadith strengthens the charge of innovation.
5
Examine the refutation of proof-texts
Al-Maturidi shows that verses about fighting and jizya apply to disbelievers, and verses of glad tidings to believers—no third group is needed.
The opponent's own scriptural evidence supports only two categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : إذ الله يقسم الأحكام أقساما ثلاثة من حيث الانقسام من اسم الكفر والإيمان وما ليس بكفر ولا إيمان حتى إذا زال حكم ذلك عنه لزم الواسط فما الدليل على أن ثمة واسط في الأسماء، بل الله في الجملة البشر المحتمل للعلم قسمين في أمر الدنيا والآخرة جميعا، فمن زاد عليه فهو المبدع في دين ما لم يؤذن له، وقد قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من آوى محدثا فعليه لعنة، فكيف بمن هو الذي أحدث الحدث، فنسأل الله العصمة واحتج بما ليسوا بكفرة بآيات قتال الكفرة وأخذ الجزية ونحو ذلك بما ليسوا بمؤمنين بأيات البشارة والولاية ونحو ذلك، فبهذا خرج عن جملة قول المؤمنين
Then we say: Since God divides rulings into three divisions from the perspective of division of the name of disbelief and faith and what is not disbelief nor faith—so that when the ruling of that is removed from him, the intermediate becomes necessary. So what is the evidence that there is an intermediate in the names? Rather, God has divided humans who are capable of knowledge into two categories in all matters of this world and the Hereafter. Whoever adds to that is an innovator in religion without permission. And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever shelters an innovator (muhdith) will be cursed by God.' So how about the one who is the inventor of the innovation? So we ask God for protection. And he argued with those who are not disbelievers by verses about fighting the disbelievers and taking the jizya and the like, and with those who are not believers by verses of glad tidings and alliance and the like. Thus he has departed from the general statement of the believers.
Source pages p. 950

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the concept of an intermediate status (wasit) between faith and disbelief in the naming. The opponent had apparently argued that God's rulings are divided into three categories: for the name of kufr, for the name of iman, and for what is neither. They then claimed that when the ruling of iman or kufr is absent, an intermediate category arises. Al-Maturidi responds by asking for evidence for such an intermediate in names. He asserts that God actually divided humans into only two categories: believers and disbelievers, in both worldly and otherworldly affairs. Adding a third category is innovation, supported by the hadith against sheltering an innovator. He then criticizes the opponent's proof-texts: verses about fighting disbelievers and taking jizya are for those who are not believers (i.e., they are disbelievers), and verses of glad tidings and alliance are for believers—so there is no third group. Thus the opponent has separated from the consensus of the believers.

Key Terms
أقسام ثلاثة
الكفر
الإيمان
الواسط
المبدع
المحدث
الجزية
البشارة
الولاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: There exists a neutral category between Muslim and non-Muslim in the afterlife or worldly rulings.
Correction: Al-Maturidi shows that God divides humans into only two groups (believers and disbelievers) in both worlds; any third category is an innovation.

Checkpoint
According to al-Maturidi, how many categories does God divide humans into?
A) Three
B) Two
C) One
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi affirms a strict binary of faith and disbelief, rejecting any intermediate category as innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever tried to create an 'in-between' category in your own heart—thinking you can enjoy some sins while still being a believer, or that doubts do not affect your faith? How does al-Maturidi's strict binary challenge you to take a definitive stand?
?
This lesson equates adding a third category to innovation. In what areas of your life have you added 'gray areas' that Islam does not recognize? Will you repent and return to the clear binary of iman and kufr?
?
Al-Maturidi says God divided humans into only two categories. When you examine your own life right now, which category do you truly belong to? What evidence from your actions and beliefs supports your answer, and are you willing to change if necessary?

Hudud and Qisas Do Not Negate Iman
Maturidi argues that hudud and qisas are expiations and do not remove iman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that carrying out hudud and qisas on a believer does not remove his iman, but rather serves as an expiation.

Core Idea
Hudud and qisas are acts of mercy that expiate sins, not signs of disbelief.

This passage addresses a crucial question: does applying Islamic penal law to a sinful believer mean that person is no longer a believer? Maturidi argues firmly that it does not. Drawing on Quranic verses and hadith, he demonstrates that hudud and qisas are expiations that actually affirm the person's faith, as they are rooted in the mercy and protection that iman entails. Let's explore his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Let the author's own argument come through before you analyse it.
Notice the compressed style and the use of proof texts.
2
Identify the key proof texts
Find the two main proofs: the hadith about protection of blood and property, and the Quranic verse about not letting pity prevent the hadd.
These are the pillars of the argument.
3
Understand the logical argument from pity
Maturidi argues that if faith were absent, pity would not be a factor; it is precisely the pity that comes from faith which could lead to neglect. The command to not let pity prevent the hadd implies faith is present.
This is a subtle but powerful point.
4
Distinguish hudud from kufr punishments
Note the contrast: punishments for disbelief lead to eternal fire, while hudud are made expiations. This underscores that hudud do not negate iman.
5
Apply the conclusion
Conclude that applying the hadd does not remove the believer from iman; it is an expiation that affirms his sanctity.
This is the central doctrinal point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما كان الثابت مما فيه الحدود والقصاص ولم له الولاية ويجب له الشهادة، وجميع ما ذكر وتقبل ويحد على ذلك، لأحد نفى الإسم بما عفى عن عذاب الله، بل ذلك كله كما قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: عصموا منى دماءهم وأموالهم إلا بحقها، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيد ذلك قوله: "وَلَا تَأْخُذْكُمْ بِهِمَا رَأْفَةٌ فِي دِينِ اللهِ"، إنه لو كان الإيمان زائلا عنه لكانت الرأفة لا تأخذه، بل رأفة الإيمان هي التي تأخذه حتى لعلها تبلغ إلى تعطيل الحد، فحدد ذلك وأيد ذلك ما لو تاب، ولا قوة إلا بالله وإقامة الحد من الرحمة لأنه يكفره ويزيل عنه. والأصل أن عقوبات الكفر لا تظهر صاحبها بل تسلمه إلى عذاب الأبد كقوله: "أغرقوا فأدخلوا نارا"، والحدود والقصاص جعلت كفارات، فثبت أنها جعلت كذلك، لم يزل الإيمان عنه.
What is established from what involves the fixed punishments and retaliation, and for him is the guardianship and testimony is obligatory, and all that is mentioned, and it is accepted and he is punished for that, for no one denies the name because of what is pardoned from the punishment of Allah. Rather all that is as he said, peace be upon him: 'Their blood and property are protected from me except by their right', and there is no power except with Allah. And that is supported by His saying: 'Let not pity for them seize you in the religion of Allah' (24:2). Indeed, if faith were removed from him, then pity would not seize him, but rather the pity of faith is what seizes him until perhaps it reaches to suspending the fixed punishment. So He determined that, and it is supported by that if he repents—and there is no power except with Allah—and the establishment of the fixed punishment is from mercy because it expiates him and removes it from him. And the principle is that the punishments of disbelief do not manifest their owner but rather deliver him to eternal punishment, as His saying: 'Drown them and cause them to enter a fire' (71:25). And the fixed punishments and retaliation have been made expiations, so it is established that they are made thus; faith does not cease from him.
Source pages p. 950

Commentary
This passage is a proof that carrying out fixed punishments (hudud) and retaliation (qisas) on a sinful believer does not negate his iman. Maturidi begins by stating that the established rulings involving hudud and qisas still carry with them guardianship and the obligation of testimony, and they are accepted from the person and he is punished. No one denies the name of iman from him because of what is pardoned from Allah's punishment. He then cites the Prophetic hadith that blood and property are protected except by right, indicating that the person still has sanctity. He supports this with the Quranic verse commanding not to let pity for the fornicators prevent carrying out the hadd (Surah al-Nur 24:2). Maturidi argues that if faith were absent from the sinner, pity would not be a factor; it is precisely the pity that comes from faith that could lead to neglect of the hadd. Therefore the command to not let pity prevent the hadd implies that faith is still present. He also notes that establishing the hadd is an act of mercy because it expiates the sin and removes its burden. He contrasts this with punishments for disbelief, which deliver the person to eternal fire. The conclusion: since hudud and qisas are made expiations, the person does not lose his iman.

Key Terms
حدود
قصاص
كفارات
إيمان
رأفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that applying the hadd removes the status of mu'min from the person.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that hudud are expiations and do not negate iman; the believer retains his faith and sanctity.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's argument, what does the Quranic verse 'Let not pity for them seize you in the religion of Allah' (24:2) imply?
A) Pity should always prevent carrying out the hadd.
B) Pity is a sign that faith is absent from the sinner.
C) Pity (based on faith) could lead to neglecting the hadd, so it is commanded against.
D) The verse is not relevant to the issue of hudud.

Key Takeaway
Hudud and qisas are expiations that do not remove a believer's iman; they affirm his sanctity and are acts of mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone being punished for a crime, do you ever think they are less of a believer? How does this lesson challenge that assumption?
?
Have you ever hesitated to support the implementation of Islamic punishments because of pity? How does Maturidi's argument about 'the pity of faith' reshape your understanding?
?
If you were to commit a sin that deserves a hadd, would you accept the punishment as an expiation? How does knowing that it does not remove your iman change your attitude toward repentance and accountability?

The Threefold Division and the Rejection of a Middle Ground
Maturidi presents a threefold division and refutes the idea of a middle ground

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's position that judgments are divided into three categories (kufr, iman, and neither) and his rejection of a middle ground between faith and disbelief.

Core Idea
There is no middle ground: Allah divides humanity into believers and disbelievers; a third category is innovation.

Maturidi begins by asserting that Allah divides judgments into three categories, but he quickly challenges the idea that this allows for a middle ground between faith and disbelief. He argues that a person must be either a believer or a disbeliever in the ultimate sense, and any claim to a third category is an innovation in religion. This passage sets the stage for debating the status of major sinners.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the overall argument. Notice the initial threefold division and the subsequent challenge.
Pay attention to the hadith about innovators and the opponent's use of Quranic verses.
2
Identify Maturidi's challenge
After presenting the three divisions, Maturidi questions the proof for a middle ground and equates adding a third category with innovation. He cites a hadith about giving refuge to an innovator.
3
Understand the opponent's argument
The opponent claims that those who are not disbelievers (major sinners) are indicated by verses about fighting disbelievers and jizya, and that they are not believers based on verses of glad tidings and guardianship. Thus, they argue for a middle category.
Maturidi presents this as a departure from the consensus of believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: إذ الله يقسم الأحكام أقساما ثلاثة من حيث الانقسام من اسم الكفر والإيمان وما ليس بكفر ولا إيمان حتى إذا زال حكم ذلك عنه لزم الواسط فما الدليل على أن ثمة واسط في الأسماء، بل الله في الجملة البشر المحتمل للعلم قسمين في أمر الدنيا والآخرة جميعا، فمن زاد عليه فهو المبدع في دين ما لم يؤذن له، وقد قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من آوى محدثا فعليه لعنة، فكيف بمن هو الذي أحدث الحدث، فنسأل الله العصمة واحتج بما ليسوا بكفرة بآيات قتال الكفرة وأخذ الجزية ونحو ذلك بما ليسوا بمؤمنين بآيات البشارة والولاية ونحو ذلك، فبهذا خرج عن جملة قول المؤمنين.
Then we say: Since Allah divides judgments into three divisions in terms of division from the name of disbelief and faith and what is neither disbelief nor faith—such that when the ruling of that is removed from him, the middle ground becomes necessary—so what is the proof that there is a middle ground in the names? Rather, Allah, in the totality of humans capable of knowledge, has two divisions in the matter of this world and the Hereafter altogether. So whoever adds to that is an innovator in the religion regarding what he has not been permitted. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever gives refuge to an innovator, upon him is the curse.' So how about the one who himself brought about the innovation? So we ask Allah for protection. And he argued by [the fact that] they are not disbelievers using verses about fighting disbelievers and taking jizya and the like, and that they are not believers using verses of glad tidings and guardianship and the like, and thus he departed from the totality of the statement of the believers.
Source pages p. 950

Commentary
This passage is a classification and a challenge. Maturidi begins by stating that Allah divides judgments (ahkam) into three categories: those that earn the name of kufr, those that earn the name of iman, and those that are neither kufr nor iman. He then presents a hypothetical: if the ruling of one of these is removed from a person, the 'middle ground' (al-wasit) follows. He demands proof for the existence of such a middle ground in the names. He then refers to humanity as being divided into two categories (believers and disbelievers) in matters of this world and the next. Adding a third category is innovation. He cites a hadith that the one who gives refuge to an innovator is cursed, and argues that the one who himself innovates is even worse. Then he mentions an opponent's argument: they say that those who are not disbelievers (i.e., major sinners) are indicated by verses about fighting disbelievers and jizya, and that they are not believers indicated by verses of glad tidings and guardianship. Therefore, the opponent claims, such a person is excluded from the totality of believers. Maturidi presents this as the opponent's departure from the consensus of the believers.

Key Terms
أقسام ثلاثة
واسط
إيمان
كفر
محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: There is a middle category between iman and kufr for major sinners who are neither believers nor disbelievers.
Correction: Maturidi argues that humanity is divided into only two groups (believers and disbelievers) in this world and the Hereafter; any third category is an innovation.

Checkpoint

A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Maturidi posits three judgment categories but rejects a middle ground, arguing that a third status between faith and disbelief is an innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Allah has divided humans into only two categories in this world and the Hereafter. Are you living as if you are in one or the other, or do you have a foot in both? What practical step can you take today to remove the 'middle ground' in your actions?
?
When the Prophet said, 'Whoever gives refuge to an innovator, upon him is the curse,' does that convict you of any innovation you have defended? Will you repent and abandon it?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
The Quranic Three Divisions Refute the Middle Ground Claim
Maturidi refutes the middle ground claim by citing the Quranic three divisions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Maturidi uses the Quranic division of humanity into believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites to refute any claim of an independent middle ground in faith, and that the only divinely recognized middle group is the hypocrites who are neither believers nor disbelievers.

Core Idea
The only middle ground in faith is the hypocrites, and they are neither believers nor disbelievers.

Maturidi here addresses a claim that there is a middle ground (wasit) in the naming of iman and kufr. He points out that the opponent's argument overlooks key considerations and then turns to the Quran itself, which clearly divides people into three categories: believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites. This refutation shows the danger of imposing human reasoning over divine classification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi begins by referencing an overlooked view, then shifts to the Quranic division.
2
Identify the two overlooked positions
Find where Maturidi mentions the view about glad tidings being conditional/final outcome and the Khawarij's two types of rulings on disbelievers. Understand why these are relevant to the opponent's claim.
3
Focus on the Quranic three divisions
Maturidi states that Allah has made clear three divisions: disbelievers, believers, and hypocrites. Note the description of hypocrites as 'oscillating between them' and being neither.
4
Understand the conclusion
Ask yourself: What happens to someone who tries to establish a middle ground that goes against the Quranic text? Maturidi says they waste the rights of division and incur hatred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كأنه أغفل عن جملة أخرى لهم وهو أن البشارة عند من يرى صاحب الكبيرة مؤمنا كانت بشريطة أو كانت هي العاقبة. وعند الخوارج كان الحكم في الكفرة على نوعين: أحدهما على القتل وأخذ الجزية والآخر لا كالنساء وأهل النفاق ونحوهم، فمن رام أن يجعل ثمة واسطا في الأحكام بما هي عند الفريقين يلزم لا بما ذكر من الواسط أغفل عن جملة قول الأمة، ولا قوة إلا بالله وهم القرآن مع ما كان الله تعالى قد بين الأقسام الثلاثة: الكفرة والمؤمنين وأهل النفاق، المذبذبون بينهما، وأخبر أنهم ليسوا من هؤلاء ولا من هؤلاء، فمن رام تثبيت الواسط لا على ما جاء به النص وأراد أن يجعله مقابلا له، على نفي الحقيقة التي جعل الله لها الواسط، فقد ضيع حقوق القسمة ونقض الترتيب الذي جاء به، فاستوجب المقت به من جميع منتحلي الإسلام.
As if he overlooked another statement of theirs: that glad tidings, with the one who sees the major sinner as a believer, were conditional or were the final outcome. And with the Khawarij, the ruling regarding disbelievers was of two types: one was killing and taking jizya, and the other was not, like women and hypocrites and the like. So whoever seeks to make there a middle ground in the rulings as they are with the two groups, it is necessary, not as the aforementioned middle ground; he overlooked the totality of the statement of the community, and there is no power except with Allah. And they are the Quran with what Allah Almighty has already made clear the three divisions: the disbelievers, the believers, and the hypocrites, oscillating between them, and He informed that they are not of these nor of those. So whoever seeks to establish the middle ground not as the text came, and wants to make it opposite to it, upon negation of the reality which Allah made for the middle ground, has wasted the rights of division and contradicted the arrangement that came with it, and thus deserved the hatred of all claimants of Islam.
Source pages p. 951

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that there is a middle ground (wasit) in the naming of iman and kufr. Maturidi points out that the opponent has neglected another view: for those who consider the major sinner a believer, glad tidings (bishara) are conditional or are the final outcome. As for the Khawarij, they divide rulings on disbelievers into two types: those subject to killing and jizya, and those not (like women and hypocrites). Thus, if one seeks to establish a middle ground based on these differing positions, it would not be the middle ground the opponent claims. Maturidi then turns to the Quran: Allah has made clear three divisions: disbelievers, believers, and hypocrites, who are 'oscillating between them' (mudhabdhabun baynahuma) and are neither. This is the only valid middle ground according to revelation. Anyone who tries to establish a different middle ground, opposing the reality Allah set for it, has wasted the rights of division and contradicted the divine arrangement, thereby deserving the hatred of all Muslims.

منافقون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some erroneously think the middle ground in faith is a separate category of belief, like a middle status between believer and disbeliever.
Correction: Maturidi shows that only the hypocrites are a Quranic middle, and they are neither believers nor disbelievers in the full sense; there is no independent third category.

Checkpoint

A) Muslims, Christians, and Jews
B) Believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites
C) Pious, sinful, and repentant
D) Angels, humans, and jinn

Key Takeaway
The Quran recognizes only three human categories regarding faith: believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites; any other middle ground is a human invention opposed to divine revelation.

How will you eliminate that compromise today?

Maturidi warns that those who establish a middle ground contrary to the Quran 'deserve the hatred of all claimants of Islam.' Ask yourself: Are there any opinions or practices you have adopted that soften the clear lines Allah has drawn between iman and kufr? What concrete step can you take to realign yourself with the Quranic divisions?
?
The Quran describes hypocrites as 'oscillating between them, not of these nor of those.' Reflect on a specific area of your faith where you waver—perhaps in prayer, charity, or dealing with worldly distractions. Refuting the Claim That Faith's Name Is Only by Revelation
Maturidi refutes the claim that naming is only by revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the claim that the name of faith (iman) is derived only from revelation, not from linguistic principles.

Core Idea
The name of faith is rooted in language, not just revelation.

In this passage, Maturidi takes on an opponent who argues that both the Murji'ah and Khawarij agree that naming faith is only by revelation, not language. Maturidi rejects this as a misrepresentation and explains the actual consensus — that linguistic reality determines the naming, and the Khawarij use language to argue that actions contradict claims of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the argument's flow become clear.
Notice the opponent's claim is introduced with 'ثم احتج' (then he argued).
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent says that both Murji'ah and Khawarij agreed that 'iman' is a name from revelation (sam'), not from linguistic analogy (qiyas). Therefore, naming can only come from scripture or consensus.
The opponent claims this is a sufficient proof (حجة كافية).
3
Understand Maturidi's response
Maturidi accuses the opponent of lying in his narration. He clarifies that both groups actually agreed that the name is realized by what language necessitates.
The key phrase: 'بل هم أجمعوا على تحقيق الاسم بما أوجبته اللغة'.
4
Connect to the Khawarij's argument
The Khawarij used the commission of major sins as evidence that the person is lying in his attestation (tasdiq), citing Quran 29:2 to show that claims are tested by actions.
This shows their argument is linguistic, not purely revelatory.
5
Reflect on the broader significance
This refutation defends the role of language in theological naming and shows that the opponent misrepresented the consensus.
Think about how this connects to the larger debate on faith and works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج بنفى اسم الكفر والإيمان عن صاحب الكبيرة، إن المرجئة والخوارج اتفقوا على أن اسم الإيمان لا يوجد بالقياس مما أوجبته اللغة، وإنما كان من جهة السمع، فلا تجوز التسمية بواحد إلا بالتواتر بالسمع أو الإجماع، وزعم أن هذه حجة كافية. قال الشيخ رحمه الله: نقول وبالله التوفيق: كذب في الحكاية عمن بلغ ذلك، بل هم أجمعوا على تحقيق الاسم بما أوجبته اللغة، لكن الخوارج استدلت بارتكاب الكبيرة على كذبه فيما أظهر من التصديق بقوله: أَحَسِبَ النَّاسُ (العنكبوت 2).
Then he argued by denying the name of disbelief and faith from the major sinner: 'Verily the Murji'ah and the Khawarij agreed that the name of faith is not derived by analogy from what language necessitates, but rather it is from revelation, so naming with any one is not permissible except by widespread transmission from revelation or consensus.' And he claimed that this is a sufficient proof. The Shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: We say, and success is from Allah: He lied in the narration from those whom that reached. Rather, they all agreed on the realization of the name by what language necessitates, but the Khawarij used the commission of major sin as evidence for his lying in what he manifested of attestation, by His saying: 'Do people think...' (29:2).
Source pages p. 951

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponent argues that both the Murji'ah and the Khawarij agree that the name 'iman' is not arrived at by linguistic analogy (al-qiyas) from what language necessitates, but only by revelation (al-sam'). Therefore, one cannot call the major sinner either a believer or a disbeliever without explicit scriptural evidence or consensus. The opponent claims this is a sufficient proof. Maturidi (referred to as 'al-Shaykh') responds by accusing the opponent of lying in his report. He says that both groups actually agreed that the name is realized based on what language necessitates (ma awjabathu al-lugha). However, the Khawarij used the fact of committing major sins as evidence that the person is lying in his professed attestation (tasdiq), citing the Quranic verse 'Do people think...' (Surah al-Ankabut 29:2), which questions whether people can claim faith without being tested. In other words, the Khawarij's position is based on a linguistic understanding that actions contradict claims, not solely on revelation.

Key Terms
مرجئة
خوارج
اسم الإيمان
قياس
سمع
لغة
كذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Both Murji'ah and Khawarij agree that the name of faith is only from revelation.
Correction: They actually agreed that the name is based on language; the Khawarij used language to argue that actions disprove faith.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, upon what did the Murji'ah and Khawarij actually agree regarding the name of iman?
A) That it is given only by revelation
B) That it is given by what language necessitates
C) That it is given by consensus
D) That it cannot be given at all

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that the dispute is not about whether language or revelation determines the name, but about how actions relate to claimed faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone's faith solely by their outward actions, forgetting that faith is linguistically a claim that may be true even if actions seem inconsistent? How does the Khawarij's error challenge your own tendency to judge others' iman?

The opponent falsely claimed a consensus to support his view. Are there beliefs you hold firmly simply because they are widely accepted, without verifying the actual scriptural and linguistic evidence? Will you commit to re-examining one such belief this week?
?
Maturidi bluntly calls the opponent's report a lie. When you defend your understanding of Islam, do you accurately represent opposing views, or do you sometimes simplify them to make your argument easier? What would it cost you to honestly state what someone else believes before rebutting it?

The Quranic Threefold Division Refutes an Intermediate Category
Maturidi cites Quranic threefold division to refute intermediate category.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quranic threefold division of believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites leaves no room for an intermediate category between faith and disbelief.

Core Idea
The Quranic threefold division closes the door to any intermediate category.

Maturidi refutes those who propose an intermediate state between belief and disbelief by invoking the Quran's own categorization of people into three groups: believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites. The Quran explicitly states that the hypocrites belong to neither group, thus any attempt to establish a separate 'middle' category distorts the divine ordering.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic division
The passage begins by stating that Allah has explained three categories: disbelievers, believers, and hypocrites who oscillate between them. Read this carefully.
2
Understand the Quranic verdict on hypocrites
The Quran says they are neither of the believers nor of the disbelievers. This is not an intermediate category but a distinct rejection.
3
Grasp the refutation
Any attempt to establish a formal intermediate category outside this division violates the divine order and deserves condemnation.
This directly refutes the idea of an intermediate state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كأنه أغفل عن جملة أخرى لهم وهو أن البشارة عند من يرى صاحب الكبيرة مؤمنا كانت بشريطة أو كانت هي العاقبة. وعند الخوارج كان الحكم فى الكفرة على نوعين: أحدهما على القتل وأخذ الجزية والآخر لا كالنساء وأهل النفاق ونحوهم، فمن رام أن يجعل ثمة واسطا في الأحكام بما هي عند الفريقين يلزم لا بما ذكر من الواسط أغفل عن جملة قول الأمة، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وهم القرآن مع ما كان الله تعالى قد بين الأقسام الثلاثة: الكفرة والمؤمنين وأهل النفاق، المذبذبون بينهما، وأخبر أنهم ليسوا من هؤلاء ولا من هؤلاء، فمن رام تثبيت الواسط لا على ما جاء به النص وأراد أن يجعله مقابلا له، على نفى الحقيقة التي جعل الله لها الواسط، فقد ضيع حقوق القسمة ونقض الترتيب الذي جاء به، فاستوجب المقت به من جميع منتحلى الاسلام، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم عارض نفسه بالمرأة فزعم أنها مخصوص، وهذا النوع من الخيال، بل أحكام الكفر مختلفة لا يستدل بها على شيء. وقد رأيته أطنب في معارضات الخوارج، وتكلف الخروج مما قابلوه به، مما يعلم اكل من تأمله أنه لم يحقق ما رام الرامى، ولا تخلص مما قوبل به حق التخلص فأغضيت عن ذكره.
It is as if he neglected another group's statement, that the good news for one who considers the committer of a major sin a believer was conditional or it was the consequence. And according to the Khawarij, the ruling regarding disbelievers was of two types: one is execution and taking of jizya, and the other is not, like women and hypocrites and the like. So whoever seeks to make an intermediate (wasit) in the rulings as they are according to the two groups must do so not based on the mentioned intermediate, neglects the statement of the community, and there is no power except with God. And [while] they [claim?] the Quran with what God Most High had explained the three categories: the disbelievers, the believers, and the hypocrites, the oscillating between them, and He informed that they are not of these nor of those. So whoever seeks to establish the intermediate not according to what the text came with and intends to make it opposite to it, in denial of the reality for which God made the intermediate, has wasted the rights of division and contradicted the order that came with it, thus deserving hatred from all adherents of Islam, and there is no power except with God. Then he objected to himself with the woman, and claimed that she is exceptional, and this kind of fantasy. Rather, the rulings of disbelief are different and cannot be used as evidence for anything. And I saw that he went on at length in objecting to the Khawarij, and burdened himself with extrication from what they confronted him with, such that anyone who contemplates it knows that he did not achieve what the aimer aimed, nor did he extricate himself from what he was confronted with properly, so I ignored mentioning it.
Source pages p. 951

Commentary
This passage is a refutation. The author begins by stating that the opponent overlooked a group's view: the good news for one who considers the major sinner a believer is conditional or only the consequence. Then he mentions the Khawarij's two types of rulings for disbelievers. The opponent seeks to establish an intermediate (wasit) based on these two groups, but the author says this is not the correct approach. He then invokes the Quranic verse that divides people into three categories: disbelievers, believers, and hypocrites who are oscillating between them. The Quran states they are neither from these nor from those. Therefore, any attempt to establish an intermediate category outside this textual division distorts the divine order and deserves condemnation. Then the author mentions that the opponent raised a self-objection regarding women, but the author dismisses this as fantasy, noting that the rulings of disbelief are varied and not evidence for the matter at hand. He then says he will not engage further with the opponent's lengthy objections to the Khawarij because they are ineffective.

Correction: The Quran does not consider hypocrites a third status; they are condemned as neither, and the threefold division is exhaustive, leaving no room for an intermediate.
