The Unknown Boundary and Its Consequences
Maturidi introduces the Mu'tazilite position and rebuts it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazilite position on the unknown boundary between sins leads to uncertainty about naming oneself a believer.

Core Idea
Uncertainty about sin boundaries makes naming oneself a believer impossible.

Imam Maturidi begins by exposing a flaw in the Mu'tazilite position: if the line between minor and major sins is unknown, then no one can be sure whether they are a believer. This undermines their insistence on suspending judgment about faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice how Maturidi starts by stating the Mu'tazilite claim.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim
Identify that the Mu'tazilites believe the boundary between minor and major sins is unknown, leading to a state of fear and hope without certainty.
This is the premise Maturidi will attack.
3
Trace Maturidi's argument
Follow how Maturidi argues that this unknown boundary creates uncertainty about both security/despair and the name of faith.
He concludes that the same uncertainty prevents both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تذكر طرفا مما يلزم المعتزلة على مذهبهم الوقف في التسمى بالإيمان، أن وهو من مذهبهم أن الحد الذي بين الصغيرة والكبيرة من المعاصي غير معروف ليكون المرء خائفا راجيا لا آمنا آيسا، فنقول: إذ لا أحد منكم يدعي براءة نفسه من كل، ولا العلم ببلوغ الحد الذي يوجب الأمن والإياس، فذلك تردد الحال بين الكبيرة والصغيرة، والكبيرة تزيل اسم الإيمان والصغيرة لحقكم الشك في اسم الإيمان وزواله كما لحقكم في اسم الكبيرة والصغيرة، فإذا منع ذلك الشك القول بالأمن والإياس، ثم لما منع التسمى بالإيمان، والذي يدفع هذين واحد، ثم لما جاز إثبات الاسم مع الخوف، وأمركم أن المؤمن لا خوف عليه، ولم يخافون من تسميتكم أنفسكم مؤمنين، الكذب الذي لعله كبيرة يزيل عنكم اسم الإيمان، فيكون بالتسمية من كبير أنفسكم، وقد حذرتم عن تزكية الأنفس بقوله تعالى: "فَلَا تُزَكُّوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ" ثم تعارضون بالبر والتقوى، أتشهدون أنفسكم بهما أو لا؟ فإن شهدوا لزمهم بالخوف في المتقين الأبرار أن يكونوا استوجبوا مقمت الله والخلود في النار. فيكون جهنم دار المتقين الأبرار لا دار الفاسقين، وقد قال الله تعالى: "إِنَّ الْأَبْرَارَ لَفِي نَعِيمٍ"، ويبطل الدعاء بقوله: "وَتَوَفَّنَا" وإن أبوا التسمية بذلك لزمهم مثله في الإيمان؛ إذ هو اسم لما به النجوة من مقت الله كالبر والتقوى. ثم يقال: إنه قد ثبت عن أنهم كانوا يدعون الله رعبا ورهبا وخوفا وطبعا ويزعمون أنهم لم يبتلوا بكبائر كان هذا الخوف مم لم يبل بها، لم لا ذلكم أن ليس ترك بيان الحد لما يخاف ويرجى، بل ذلك لما لله معاقبة من شاء بالصغائر. ومن قولكم: إن ما يوجب العقوبة يزيل اسم الإيمان، فاعتبروا بأن لستم مؤمنين على ما أخبرتم في الحقيقة، والله الموفق. وقد قال الله تعالى: "إِنَّمَا الْمُؤْمِنِينَ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِاللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَرْتَابُوا" وعندكم المؤمن لا يخاف نقمة الله ولا يرجو رحمته، بل قد استوجب رحمته لو كان مؤمنا وليس لله أن يعذبه لو كان مؤمنا، والإيمان هو الذي حملهم على ذلك، فكيف الزمتموهم الخوف؟ وذلك ليس على المؤمن في الحقيقة، ومنعتموهم على الارتياب في الإيمان، والارتياب فيه بما رأى الخوف: وذلك بين التناقض، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then mention a portion of what necessarily follows for the Mu'tazilites from their position of suspending judgment regarding being called believers—and it is part of their position that the boundary between minor and major sins is unknown, so that a person may be fearful and hopeful, not secure and despairing. So we say: Since none of you claims innocence from everything, nor knowledge of reaching the boundary that necessitates security and despair, thus the situation oscillates between major and minor sin. The major sin removes the name of faith, and the minor sin—you are uncertain about the name of faith and its removal, just as you are uncertain about the name of major and minor. So when that uncertainty prevents the assertion of security and despair, and then it prevents being called believers—and that which repels both is one—then when it is permissible to affirm the name with fear, and your command that the believer has no fear, are you not afraid that by naming yourselves believers (the lie which might be a major sin) would remove from you the name of faith, so that by naming you become among your major sins? And you have been warned against self-purification by His statement: "Do not purify yourselves." Then you adduce righteousness and piety. Do you testify to yourselves for them or not? If they testify, then fear would necessitate for the righteous and pious that they have deserved God's wrath and eternal punishment in the Fire. Thus Hell would be the abode of the righteous and pious, not of the wicked. And God Almighty said: "Indeed the righteous are in bliss." And the supplication "And cause us to die" would be invalidated. And if they refuse to call themselves by that, the same applies to faith, for it is a name for what saves from God's wrath, like righteousness and piety. Then it is said: It is established that they used to call upon God with reverence, awe, fear, and supplication, and they claimed they were not afflicted with major sins. Was this fear because they were not afflicted? No, that is not leaving the explanation of the boundary of what is feared and hoped; rather that is because God may punish whomever He wills for minor sins. And from your statement: "What necessitates punishment removes the name of faith." So consider that you are not believers in reality according to what you have been told. And God is the Grantor of success. And God Almighty said: "The believers are only those who have believed in God and His Messenger and then have not doubted." Yet according to you, the believer does not fear God's punishment nor hope for His mercy; rather he has deserved His mercy if he is a believer, and God cannot punish him if he is a believer. Faith is what drove them to that. So how do you impose fear upon them? That is not upon the believer in reality. And you prevent them from doubt in faith, while doubt in it occurs due to fear. That is clear contradiction. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 963

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position on naming oneself a believer and the role of fear. Imam Maturidi argues against the Mu'tazilite claim that the boundary between minor and major sins is unknown, which they use to justify a state of fear and hope without certainty. He points out that if the boundary is unknown, one cannot be secure about faith, and this uncertainty prevents both security and despair as well as the naming of oneself as a believer. He then challenges them: if it is permissible to affirm the name 'believer' with fear, why do they command that the believer has no fear? Calling oneself a believer without fear might be a lie, which could be a major sin removing the name of faith. He quotes the verse 'Do not purify yourselves' to caution against self-praise. He further argues that if they claim righteousness and piety for themselves, they would have to fear wrath and hell, contradicting the Qur'anic promise that the righteous are in bliss. This inconsistency applies similarly to faith. He then notes that even prophets called upon God with fear despite not committing major sins, showing that fear does not negate faith. Finally, he exposes a contradiction: according to Mu'tazilites, the believer does not fear punishment, yet they acknowledge that fear can cause doubt in faith, which is a contradiction. The argument is structured as a dialectical refutation, moving point by point.

Key Terms
الحد
الكبيرة
الصغيرة
التسمى بالإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilites thought that suspending judgment about faith is a rational position.
Correction: Maturidi shows that their premise about the unknown boundary leads to logical consequences that undermine their ability to name themselves believers at all.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the Mu'tazilite claim about the unknown boundary between sins lead to?
A) It allows believers to be secure in their faith.
B) It creates uncertainty that prevents both security/despair and naming oneself a believer.
C) It only affects major sins, not minor ones.
D) It has no effect on the naming of faith.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite assumption of an unknown sin-boundary leads to an inability to claim faith with certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own sins, do you ever assume you know which ones are major? How does this lesson expose the danger of assuming you can categorize your sins without a certain boundary? What would you need to change in how you assess your spiritual state?
?
If you were truly uncertain about the boundary between major and minor sins, would it make you more cautious or more confused? Are you willing to admit that you cannot be sure of your own faith status, or do you secretly assume you are safe? How does that assumption affect your relationship with Allah?
?
The Mu'tazilites wanted a balanced state of fear and hope, but Maturidi showed that without a known boundary, both fear and hope become impossible. Where in your life do you rely on an unknown standard to avoid facing the full weight of your actions? Will you now seek clarity from revelation rather than ignorance?

Fear, Self-Purification, and the Prophets' Example
Maturidi challenges the Mu'tazilite view on fear and uses examples to refute it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses the prophets' fear and the Qur'anic prohibition of self-purification to refute the Mu'tazilite position that the believer must not fear.

Core Idea
Even prophets feared, so fear does not negate faith.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi shifts to challenge the Mu'tazilite command that the believer must be free from fear. He points out that calling oneself a believer out of fear might be a lie, and that even prophets feared God. He also invokes the Qur'anic verse 'Do not purify yourselves' to caution against self-praise.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the multiple arguments Maturidi presents.
This section contains several sub-arguments.
2
Identify the challenge about fear
Find where Maturidi questions why the Mu'tazilites command no fear if they allow naming oneself a believer with fear.
He asks: aren't you afraid that calling yourselves believers might be a lie and a major sin?
3
Understand the argument about self-purification
See how Maturidi uses the verse 'Do not purify yourselves' to argue against self-testimony of faith.
This applies to both faith and righteousness/piety.
4
Learn from the prophets' example
Note that even prophets called upon God with fear, showing that fear does not remove faith.
This refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that fear is incompatible with faith.

ثم تذكر طرفا مما يلزم المعتزلة على مذهبهم الوقف في التسمى بالإيمان، أن وهو من مذهبهم أن الحد الذي بين الصغيرة والكبيرة من المعاصي غير معروف ليكون المرء خائفا راجيا لا آمنا آيسا، فنقول: إذ لا أحد منكم يدعي براءة نفسه من كل، ولا العلم ببلوغ الحد الذي يوجب الأمن والإياس، فذلك تردد الحال بين الكبيرة والصغيرة، والكبيرة تزيل اسم الإيمان والصغيرة لحقكم الشك في اسم الإيمان وزواله كما لحقكم في اسم الكبيرة والصغيرة، فإذا منع ذلك الشك القول بالأمن والإياس، ثم لما منع التسمى بالإيمان، والذي يدفع هذين واحد، ثم لما جاز إثبات الاسم مع الخوف، وأمركم أن المؤمن لا خوف عليه، ولم يخافون من تسميتكم أنفسكم مؤمنين، الكذب الذي لعله كبيرة يزيل عنكم اسم الإيمان، فيكون بالتسمية من كبير أنفسكم، وقد حذرتم عن تزكية الأنفس بقوله تعالى: "فَلَا تُزَكُّوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ" ثم تعارضون بالبر والتقوى، أتشهدون أنفسكم بهما أو لا؟ فإن شهدوا لزمهم بالخوف في المتقين الأبرار أن يكونوا استوجبوا مقمت الله والخلود في النار. فيكون جهنم دار المتقين الأبرار لا دار الفاسقين، وقد قال الله تعالى: "إِنَّ الْأَبْرَارَ لَفِي نَعِيمٍ"، ويبطل الدعاء بقوله: "وَتَوَفَّنَا" وإن أبوا التسمية بذلك لزمهم مثله في الإيمان؛ إذ هو اسم لما به النجوة من مقت الله كالبر والتقوى. ثم يقال: إنه قد ثبت عن أنهم كانوا يدعون الله رعبا ورهبا وخوفا وطبعا ويزعمون أنهم لم يبتلوا بكبائر كان هذا الخوف مم لم يبل بها، لم لا ذلكم أن ليس ترك بيان الحد لما يخاف ويرجى، بل ذلك لما لله معاقبة من شاء بالصغائر. ومن قولكم: إن ما يوجب العقوبة يزيل اسم الإيمان، فاعتبروا بأن لستم مؤمنين على ما أخبرتم في الحقيقة، والله الموفق. وقد قال الله تعالى: "إِنَّمَا الْمُؤْمِنِينَ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِاللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَرْتَابُوا" وعندكم المؤمن لا يخاف نقمة الله ولا يرجو رحمته، بل قد استوجب رحمته لو كان مؤمنا وليس لله أن يعذبه لو كان مؤمنا، والإيمان هو الذي حملهم على ذلك، فكيف الزمتموهم الخوف؟ وذلك ليس على المؤمن في الحقيقة، ومنعتموهم على الارتياب في الإيمان، والارتياب فيه بما رأى الخوف: وذلك بين التناقض، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then mention a portion of what necessarily follows for the Mu'tazilites from their position of suspending judgment regarding being called believers—and it is part of their position that the boundary between minor and major sins is unknown, so that a person may be fearful and hopeful, not secure and despairing. So we say: Since none of you claims innocence from everything, nor knowledge of reaching the boundary that necessitates security and despair, thus the situation oscillates between major and minor sin. The major sin removes the name of faith, and the minor sin—you are uncertain about the name of faith and its removal, just as you are uncertain about the name of major and minor. So when that uncertainty prevents the assertion of security and despair, and then it prevents being called believers—and that which repels both is one—then when it is permissible to affirm the name with fear, and your command that the believer has no fear, are you not afraid that by naming yourselves believers (the lie which might be a major sin) would remove from you the name of faith, so that by naming you become among your major sins? And you have been warned against self-purification by His statement: "Do not purify yourselves." Then you adduce righteousness and piety. Do you testify to yourselves for them or not? If they testify, then fear would necessitate for the righteous and pious that they have deserved God's wrath and eternal punishment in the Fire. Thus Hell would be the abode of the righteous and pious, not of the wicked. And God Almighty said: "Indeed the righteous are in bliss." And the supplication "And cause us to die" would be invalidated. And if they refuse to call themselves by that, the same applies to faith, for it is a name for what saves from God's wrath, like righteousness and piety. Then it is said: It is established that they used to call upon God with reverence, awe, fear, and supplication, and they claimed they were not afflicted with major sins. Was this fear because they were not afflicted? No, that is not leaving the explanation of the boundary of what is feared and hoped; rather that is because God may punish whomever He wills for minor sins. And from your statement: "What necessitates punishment removes the name of faith." So consider that you are not believers in reality according to what you have been told. And God is the Grantor of success. And God Almighty said: "The believers are only those who have believed in God and His Messenger and then have not doubted." Yet according to you, the believer does not fear God's punishment nor hope for His mercy; rather he has deserved His mercy if he is a believer, and God cannot punish him if he is a believer. Faith is what drove them to that. So how do you impose fear upon them? That is not upon the believer in reality. And you prevent them from doubt in faith, while doubt in it occurs due to fear. That is clear contradiction. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 963

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position on naming oneself a believer and the role of fear. Imam Maturidi argues against the Mu'tazilite claim that the boundary between minor and major sins is unknown, which they use to justify a state of fear and hope without certainty. He points out that if the boundary is unknown, one cannot be secure about faith, and this uncertainty prevents both security and despair as well as the naming of oneself as a believer. He then challenges them: if it is permissible to affirm the name 'believer' with fear, why do they command that the believer has no fear? Calling oneself a believer without fear might be a lie, which could be a major sin removing the name of faith. He quotes the verse 'Do not purify yourselves' to caution against self-praise. He further argues that if they claim righteousness and piety for themselves, they would have to fear wrath and hell, contradicting the Qur'anic promise that the righteous are in bliss. This inconsistency applies similarly to faith. He then notes that even prophets called upon God with fear despite not committing major sins, showing that fear does not negate faith. Finally, he exposes a contradiction: according to Mu'tazilites, the believer does not fear punishment, yet they acknowledge that fear can cause doubt in faith, which is a contradiction. The argument is structured as a dialectical refutation, moving point by point.

Key Terms
الخوف
تزكية الأنفس
البر
التقوى
الكبير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That fear of punishment necessarily negates faith.
Correction: Maturidi shows that even prophets feared God, so fear and faith can coexist.

Checkpoint
How does the example of the prophets refute the Mu'tazilite view on fear?
A) The prophets never feared God.
B) The prophets feared God despite not committing major sins, showing fear does not negate faith.
C) The prophets only feared major sins.
D) The prophets were secure from all fear.

Key Takeaway
Fear of God is not incompatible with faith; even prophets feared.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel fear of Allah's punishment, do you interpret that as weakness in your faith, or as a call to draw closer to Him? What would change if you saw that fear as a gift rather than a deficiency?
?
The prophets, despite their rank, cried out to Allah in fear. Is your fear of Allah directed toward avoiding His displeasure in your daily choices? Or is it a passive anxiety that leads nowhere?
?
If you had to stand before Allah tonight and He asked you, 'Did you fear Me?' would your answer be a testimony of love or of neglect? How will you turn your fear into action tomorrow?

The Clear Contradiction in Mu'tazilite Doctrine
Maturidi concludes with a logical contradiction in Mu'tazilite thought.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize the logical contradiction in the Mu'tazilite position that the believer must not fear punishment yet fear can cause doubt in faith.

Core Idea
If fear causes doubt and doubt removes faith, then the believer cannot fear.

In the final part, Imam Maturidi exposes a direct contradiction: the Mu'tazilites say the believer does not fear, but they also say fear can lead to doubt, which removes faith. This inconsistency undermines their entire position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the final argument.
Note the Qur'anic verse quoted.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim about the believer
Find where Maturidi states that according to the Mu'tazilites, the believer does not fear punishment and has deserved mercy.
This is their doctrine.
3
Find the contradiction
See how Maturidi points out that the Mu'tazilites also say fear causes doubt, which removes faith, yet they deny fear for believers.
This is the final refutation.

?

?

Faith Does Not Eliminate Fear: Maturidi's Critique
Maturidi critiques a view that denies the believer's fear and hope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that faith does not remove the believer's fear of God's punishment, and how he exposes a contradiction in the opposing view.

Core Idea
Faith removes doubt, not fear – a key distinction in Maturidi's theology.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi confronts a theological error: the claim that a true believer cannot fear God's punishment or hope for His mercy. He uses a Quranic verse to show that the verse actually speaks about doubt, not fear. He then argues that the opponents' position is internally contradictory. This lesson unpacks his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text from the source, then compare with the translation. Notice the verse quoted and the argument that follows.
2
Identify the opponent's view
From the text, what do the opponents claim about the believer's relationship with fear and hope? Write it down.
They claim the believer does not fear punishment nor hope for mercy.
3
Understand Maturidi's use of the verse
Maturidi quotes Qur'an 49:15. Does this verse support the opponent's view? Why does Maturidi think they misinterpret it?
The verse mentions doubt, not fear.
4
See the contradiction
Maturidi points out that the opponents deny fear but also prohibit doubt in faith. Explain why this is contradictory.
They consider fear as a sign of doubt, yet they deny fear and forbid doubt.
5
Reflect on the implication
What does this teach us about the relationship between faith and emotional states like fear and hope?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال الله تعالى: إِنَّمَا المُؤْمِنِينَ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِاللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَرْتَابُوا ١٤ وعندكم المؤمن لا يخاف نقمة الله ولا يرجو رحمته، بل قد استوجب رحمته لو كان مؤمنا وليس لله أن يعذبه لو كان مؤمنا، والإيمان هو الذي حملهم على ذلك، فكيف الزمتموهم الخوف؟ وذلك ليس على المؤمن في الحقيقة، ومنعتموهم على الارتياب فى الإيمان، والارتياب فيه بما رأى الخوف: وذلك بين التناقض، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And Allah the Exalted said: 'The believers are only those who believed in Allah and His Messenger then did not doubt' [49:15]. And according to you, the believer does not fear Allah's punishment nor hope for His mercy, but rather he has certainly deserved His mercy if he is a believer, and Allah has no right to punish him if he is a believer. And faith is what carried them to that. So how do you necessitate fear for them? That is not upon the believer in reality, and you prevented them from doubt in faith, and doubt in it due to what is seen of fear — that is manifest contradiction. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 964

Commentary
This passage is a critique of a position that denies the believer's fear of God's punishment and hope for His mercy, based on the verse that believers do not doubt. The author (Maturidi) argues that the verse does not negate fear; rather, it negates doubt in faith. He points out the contradiction in the opponents' view: they deny fear for the believer but also claim that faith necessitates no fear. He concludes that this is contradictory.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الخوف
النقمة
الرحمة
الارتياب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A true believer should never fear God's punishment or hope for His mercy because faith guarantees paradise.
Correction: Maturidi shows that faith removes doubt, not fear; the believer can and should fear Allah's punishment and hope for His mercy, as this is part of faith.

Checkpoint
What contradiction does the author point out in the opponents' view?
A) They believe in intercession but deny it.
B) They deny fear for the believer but also claim that faith prevents doubt, yet fear is not doubt.
C) They affirm the verse but reject its interpretation.
D) They mix up major and minor sins.

Key Takeaway
Faith removes doubt, not fear; denying fear leads to contradiction with the prohibition of doubt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever console yourself with the thought, 'I am a believer, so Allah will surely forgive me and not punish me'? How does Maturidi's critique of the opponents' view expose the danger of such an assumption, and what will you do to replace that complacency with a balanced hope and fear?
?
Do you find it easier to focus on Allah's mercy and neglect His punishment? In light of this lesson, how would you adjust your daily worship to ensure you are not falling into the contradiction of denying fear while claiming faith?
?
The Quran defines believers as those who do not doubt. Examine your own heart: are there areas where you have false certainty—thinking you are safe from Allah's punishment—that actually masks a lack of true faith? What concrete step can you take today to cultivate both hope and fear in your relationship with Allah?

Who Raises the Objection? Identifying the Source
Maturidi identifies the source of the objection as obsessive whispers, not legitimate theological groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi excludes the Khawarij and Mu'tazila from this objection and identifies the 'obsessives' as its source.

Core Idea
Not all objections come from known sects; some are whispered by shaytan to cause doubt.

Before addressing the objection itself, Maturidi first clarifies who is raising it. This is a critical methodological step—by identifying the source, he shows that the question is not a genuine theological problem from established groups but a whisper from shaytan meant to destabilize faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first sentence where the objector argues that everything contrary to God is done at shaytan's call and thus constitutes obedience to him.
Notice the logic: if every sin pleases shaytan, then by doing it you are obeying him.
2
Identify Maturidi's response to the objector's identity
Maturidi says the question is not from the Khawarij or Mu'tazila, but from 'some obsessives' (al-muswaswisin). Understand why he excludes the two groups.
The Khawarij and Mu'tazila accept that prophets and righteous people can err, so this objection would not apply to them.
3
Reflect on the purpose of this identification
By labeling the objector, Maturidi disarms the argument: it is not a valid theological inquiry but a temptation (waswasa) that can lead to unbelief.
This is a protective measure for the believer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال قائل : إذا كان كل خلاف الله فهو مما دعا إليه الشيطان ويستر به ، لم لا صار ذلك طاعة له ، ومَنْ فَعَل فعلاً لطاعة الشيطان يكفر يصير به عابدا له ؛ إذ ذلك منه وضع شرع مقابل لشرع الله وداع إليه ، عبد الشيطان فقد بين الله منازل عباد الشيطان
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : ليست هذه المسألة للخوارج والمعتزلة لإقرارهم في الأنبياء بالزال والأخيار ، لكنها لبعض الموسوسين ، يوسوس إليهم الشيطان هذا ؛ ليكفرهم بهذا ؛ إذ ذلك معلوم أنه من تزيين الشيطان وما دعا إليه ، فيصيرون قولهم مطيعين له كفار ، نسأل الله العصمة عنه
على
نقول فى ذلك بوجوه : أحدها أن ليس فى ذلك طاعة للشيطان وإن كان هو يسر به ويتلذذ لشوم طبعه وسوء اختياره ؛ إذ لم يكن الذي يتعاطاه بفعله لأمره ودعائه إليه ، والطاعة هي التي تؤدى على الأمر لا على ما يسر ويتلذذ ؛ لأن للعباد فيما أعطاهم الله الشهوات لذات و سرورا ، ومحال وصف الله بالطاعة لهم ، أو يمكن الأمر منهم إياه بالفعل ، دل أن ليس ذلك الوجه هو سبيل معرفة الطاعة ، ولا قوة إلا بالله والثانى أن الديانات من اعتقادات لا أفعال تكتسب ، إذ الاعتقادات لا يجرى عليها القهر والغلبة ، ولا لأحد من الخلائق على اعتقاد آخر ومنعه سلطان ، ومن أفعال القلوب خاصة ، وربما كان للألسن بها تعلق من حيث لا يقدر على استعمال لسان غيره وكذلك قلبه ، ويقدر على سائر الجوارح . وإذا كانت الديانات ما ذكرنا ، والكفر والإيمان دين ، لم يصر الذي ذكرت لو كان طاعة ديناً والكفر دين ، فكيف وهو من الوجه الذى ذكرت ليس بطاعة . وقد روى عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه أجاب لهذا السؤال أن الذى ذكرته حق القصد لا حق الوقوع على حال لا يقصد ذلك ، وعلى ذلك أمور علقت بالقصد ، وذلك يخرج على ما بينا من ترتيب الاعتقادات ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And one said: If everything contrary to God is something that shaytan calls to and is pleased by, why is that not obedience to him? And whoever does an action for obedience to shaytan becomes an unbeliever, becoming thereby a worshiper of him, because that would be setting up a law (shar') opposed to God's law and calling to it, and he has worshiped shaytan. God has made clear the stations of the worshipers of shaytan. Abu Mansur (Maturidi), may God have mercy on him, said: This question does not apply to the Khawarij and Mu'tazila because they acknowledge the possibility of error in prophets and the righteous, but it is for some of the obsessives (al-muswaswisin); shaytan whispers this to them to cause them to become unbelievers by it, because it is known that it is from shaytan's adornment and what he calls to, so they become, by their statement, obedient to him and unbelievers. We ask God for protection from it. We say regarding that with several aspects: First, that there is no obedience to shaytan in that, even if he is pleased by it and delights due to the evil of his nature and his bad choice, because what one undertakes is not done by his command and call. Obedience is that which is performed upon command, not upon what pleases and delights. For the servants have, in what God has given them of desires, pleasures and joys, and it is impossible to describe God as being obedient to them, nor can they command Him to act. This indicates that this aspect is not the way of knowing obedience. There is no power except through God. Second, that religions (al-diyanat) are beliefs (i'tiqadat), not acquired actions, because beliefs are not subject to coercion and dominance, nor does any creature have power over another's belief or to prevent it. They are specifically actions of the heart. Sometimes tongues are connected to them in that one cannot use another's tongue, nor his heart, though he can control other limbs. Since religions are as we have stated, and unbelief and faith are religion, what you mentioned, even if it were obedience, would not become a religion while unbelief is a religion, so how is it when from the aspect you mentioned it is not obedience? And it has been narrated from Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, that he answered this question: what you mentioned is about the truth of intention (qasd), not the truth of occurrence when one does not intend that. And on that basis matters are linked to intention. And that follows what we have explained about the ordering of beliefs. There is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 967

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection that any action contrary to God, since it is called to and pleased by shaytan, would constitute obedience to shaytan and thus unbelief. The author first identifies the source of this objection as coming from the obsessives (موسوسين), not the Khawarij or Mu'tazila, because the latter admit that prophets and the righteous can err. The response has two main aspects. First, obedience is defined by acting on command, not by pleasing or delighting. Even if shaytan is pleased, the action is not done by his command, so it is not obedience. The author analogizes: God gives humans desires and pleasures, but that does not mean humans are obeying God by enjoying them, nor can God be described as obeying humans. Second, religions are about beliefs (اعتقادات), not acquired actions. Beliefs cannot be coerced; they are internal acts of the heart. External actions of the limbs are distinct. Since unbelief and faith are religions (belief systems), even if the action were considered obedience, it would not constitute a religion. But in fact it is not obedience at all, as established in the first aspect. Finally, the author narrates from Abu Hanifa that the issue is about intention (قصد): if one does not intend to obey shaytan, the action does not become obedience. Thus, the entire matter is tied to the ordering of beliefs (ترتيب الاعتقادات), which underscores that unbelief is a matter of inner conviction, not merely external actions.

Key Terms
الموسوسين
الخوارج
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all sins make one an unbeliever because they please shaytan.
Correction: Maturidi shows that this very reasoning is a whisper from shaytan, and not a valid theological argument. The Khawarij and Mu'tazila do not hold this view.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, from which group does this objection actually come?
A) The Khawarij
B) The Mu'tazila
C) Some obsessives (al-muswaswisin)
D) The philosophers

Key Takeaway
Maturidi identifies the objection as a shaytanic whisper, not a genuine theological question, thereby protecting believers from self-condemnation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your own sins make you no longer a believer? Where did that thought come from? In light of this lesson, how can you respond to that whisper?
?
When a doubt about your faith enters your mind, do you investigate its source? This lesson shows that some doubts are not from logical inquiry but from shaytan. Will you now pause and ask, 'Who is speaking?' before accepting it?
?
Maturidi ends with a prayer for protection. Do you have a habit of turning to Allah when whispers come, or do you entertain them? What specific step will you take today to guard against waswasa?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
4 min
The First Aspect: Obedience is by Command, Not by Pleasing
Maturidi presents the first aspect of his response: obedience is defined by command, not by pleasing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's first argument: that obedience is defined by acting on command, not by whether the action pleases or delights the one being followed.

Core Idea
Obedience requires intentional command; pleasing alone does not constitute obedience.

Having identified the source of the objection, Maturidi now offers a direct refutation. The first aspect focuses on the nature of obedience itself. He argues that an action cannot be called 'obedience' simply because it pleases shaytan; true obedience requires that the action be performed in response to his command.

Guided Path
1
Read the first aspect passage
Read the Arabic text starting from 'نقول فى ذلك بوجوه : أحدها' to 'ولا قوة إلا بالله'. Notice how Maturidi defines obedience.
The key phrase: 'والطاعة هي التي تؤدى على الأمر'.
2
Analyze the definition of obedience
Obedience is defined as action upon command (على الأمر). Actions that merely please or delight are not obedience, even if the one pleased is delighted.
Maturidi uses the analogy of God giving desires: God is not obeyed when we enjoy them, nor is God described as obeying us.
3
Apply to the objection
Even if shaytan is pleased by a disobedient act, that act is not done by his command, so it is not obedience to him. Therefore, the objector's conclusion (that it makes one an unbeliever) is invalid.
This is a clear logical refutation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's first aspect, what is the defining characteristic of obedience (طاعة)?
A) It pleases the one being obeyed.
B) It is done by command of the one being obeyed.
C) It is done consistently.
D) It is visible to others.

Key Takeaway
Obedience is defined by acting on command, not by pleasing; thus, acts that please shaytan without his command are not obedience to him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you do something that pleases people but is not commanded by Allah, do you consider it obedience to them? How does this lesson challenge the way you define obedience in your relationships?
?
Are there areas in your life where you have prioritized pleasing yourself or others over obeying Allah's clear commands? What is one specific command of Allah you have been neglecting because it doesn't 'feel' pleasurable?
?
This lesson says obedience is by command, not by pleasing. How does that affect your worship? Is your prayer, fasting, or charity done because Allah commanded it, or because it makes you feel good? Will you commit to checking your intention before every act of worship today?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate

The Second Aspect: Religions are Beliefs, Not Actions
Maturidi presents the second aspect: religions are based on beliefs, not actions, and intention is key.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's second argument: that religions (including unbelief and faith) are based on beliefs (اعتقادات), not on external actions, and that intention plays a crucial role.

Core Idea
Unbelief is a matter of inner belief, not external actions, and is tied to intention.

Maturidi's second aspect shifts the focus from actions to beliefs. He argues that religions—including unbelief and faith—are fundamentally about inner convictions, not acquired actions. External actions can be coerced, but belief cannot. He also reports Abu Hanifa's point that intention (قصد) is essential: if one does not intend to obey shaytan, the action does not become obedience.

Guided Path
1
Read the second aspect passage
Read from 'والثانى' to the end. Note the key claim: 'الديانات من اعتقادات لا أفعال تكتسب'.
2
Understand the nature of beliefs
Beliefs (اعتقادات) are internal and cannot be coerced or controlled by others. They are actions of the heart, not of the limbs.
The external limbs can be forced, but the heart cannot.
3
Apply to the objection
Since unbelief is a religion (belief system), even if an action were considered obedience, it would not be the religion of unbelief unless the belief is present. Moreover, it is not obedience at all as shown in the first aspect.
4
Consider the role of intention
Abu Hanifa adds that the objector's point only applies if one intends (قصد) to obey shaytan. Without intention, it is not obedience.
This ties back to the ordering of beliefs.

According to the second aspect, what are religions (الديانات) based on?
A) External actions that can be seen

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever performed an outward act of obedience while your heart was indifferent or even reluctant? In light of this lesson, what does that reveal about the true state of your faith? Will you commit to examining your intentions before every action from now on?
?
If unbelief is ultimately a matter of inner belief and intention, then what is the condition of your heart right now? Are you truly convinced of the Oneness of Allah at the deepest level, or do you rely on external rituals to feel secure? What will you do to strengthen your inner conviction today?
?
This lesson teaches that no one can force another's belief, and that each person is personally accountable for their own heart. Do you judge others based on their external actions alone, forgetting that only Allah knows their true beliefs? How can you change your attitude to be more merciful and less presumptuous, starting with one person you are prone to judge?

The Source of Doubt: Whisperings of Shaytan
Imam Maturidi introduces a doubt and identifies its origin as whisperings from Shaytan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that certain theological doubts about obedience to Allah are not valid inquiries but originate from Shaytan's whisperings, and how Imam Maturidi identifies their source and purpose.

Core Idea
Some doubts are not questions—they are traps from Shaytan.

Imam Maturidi addresses a provocative doubt: if every sin is obedience to Shaytan, does that mean every sinner becomes a disbeliever? He does not engage the argument on its own terms but instead traces its origin to whisperings from Shaytan aimed at making people fall into disbelief. This lesson explores how the Imam diagnoses the source of such doubts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the flow from the question to the Imam's response.
2
Identify the doubt and its refutation
What is the doubt? How does the Imam respond? Who does he say raises this doubt?
3
Reflect on the danger of whisperings
Why does the Imam seek Allah's protection? How can recognizing the source of a doubt protect one's faith?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال قائل : إذا كان كل خلاف الله فهو مما دعا إليه الشيطان ويستر به ، لم لا صار ذلك طاعة له ، ومَنْ فَعَل فعلاً لطاعة الشيطان يكفر يصير به عابدا له ؛ إذ ذلك منه وضع شرع مقابل لشرع الله وداع إليه ، عبد الشيطان فقد بين الله منازل عباد الشيطان. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : ليست هذه المسألة للخوارج والمعتزلة لإقرارهم في الأنبياء بالزال والأخيار ، لكنها لبعض الموسوسين لكنها لبعض الموسوسين ، يوسوس إليهم الشيطان هذا ؛ ليكفرهم بهذا ؛ إذ ذلك معلوم أنه من تزيين الشيطان وما دعا إليه ، فيصيرون قولهم مطيعين له كفار ، نسأل الله العصمة عنه
And a questioner said: If every opposition to Allah is something the devil calls to and takes pleasure in, why is that not obedience to him? And whoever performs an act for obedience to the devil becomes a disbeliever and thereby becomes a worshipper of him, since that constitutes establishing a law in opposition to Allah's law and calling to it, he has worshipped the devil. Indeed Allah has made known the stations of the worshippers of the devil. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: This question is not for the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, because they affirm [some] error in the prophets and the righteous, but it is for some whisperers, to whom the devil whispers this in order to cause them to disbelieve by it; for it is known that it is from the devil's embellishment and what he calls to, so they become, by their statement, obedient to him and disbelievers. We ask Allah for protection from it.
Source pages p. 968

Commentary
This passage presents a theological doubt and identifies its source. The questioner argues that any act of disobedience to Allah is actually obedience to Shaytan and therefore constitutes worship of Shaytan, leading to disbelief. Imam al-Maturidi responds that such a doubt does not come from the Khawarij or Mu'tazila, who already have flawed views about prophets, but from certain individuals who are whispered to by Shaytan. The purpose of this whispering is to make them disbelieve by accepting this reasoning. The Imam concludes by seeking Allah's protection from such whisperings.

The true source of some doubts is not reason but devilish whisperings aiming to cause disbelief.

Obedience Defined by Command, Not Pleasure
Imam Maturidi defines obedience as action upon command, rejecting pleasure as criterion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that obedience in Islamic theology is defined by acting upon command, not by causing pleasure or delight.

Core Idea
Obedience is doing what is commanded, not what pleases.

Imam Maturidi addresses a subtle question: If a sinner's action pleases Shaytan, does that make it obedience to Shaytan? He argues no, because obedience is defined by following a command, not by resulting pleasure. This passage establishes a key principle for understanding moral responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Then read the English translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice how Imam Maturidi begins with 'نقول فى ذلك بوجوه' indicating multiple aspects.
2
Identify the definition of obedience
Find the sentence that defines obedience. It is the key claim: 'والطاعة هي التي تؤدى على الأمر'.
3
Understand the argument
Notice how the author uses the definition to refute the idea that pleasing Shaytan counts as obedience. He also notes that desires and pleasures are natural and not obedience, and that it is impossible for Allah to be obedient.
This argument shows that the criterion for obedience is the command, not the outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نقول فى ذلك بوجوه : أحدها أن ليس فى ذلك طاعة للشيطان وإن كان هو يسر به ويتلذذ لشوم طبعه وسوء اختياره ؛ إذ لم يكن الذي يتعاطاه بفعله لأمره ودعائه إليه ، والطاعة هى التي تؤدى على الأمر لا على ما يسر ويتلذذ ؛ لأن للعباد فيما أعطاهم الله الشهوات لذات و سرورا ، ومحال وصف الله بالطاعة لهم ، أو يمكن الأمر منهم إياه بالفعل ، دل أن ليس ذلك الوجه هو سبيل معرفة الطاعة ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
We say concerning that in several aspects: One of them is that there is in that no obedience to the devil, even if he is pleased by it and delights in it due to the wickedness of his nature and his evil choice, because what one undertakes by his action is not done by his command and call. Obedience is what is performed upon command, not upon what pleases and delights. For servants have, in what Allah has given them of desires, pleasures and delights, and it is impossible to describe Allah as being obedient to them, or for them to command Him with an action. This indicates that this aspect is not the way of recognizing obedience. And there is no power except through Allah.
Source pages p. 968

Commentary
This passage is a definition and argument. It begins by stating that the first aspect of the answer is that there is no obedience to Shaytan in a sinful action, even if Shaytan is pleased by it. The reason is that obedience is defined as performing an action in response to a command. Since the sinner did not act upon Shaytan's command, the action cannot be called obedience to him. The author further argues that desires and pleasures are natural and do not constitute obedience to anyone. It is also impossible to conceive of Allah being obedient to His servants. Therefore, pleasure or delight is not the criterion for obedience.

Key Terms
طاعة
أمر
شهوة
شيطان
لذة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any action pleasing to Shaytan is obedience to him.
Correction: Obedience requires acting upon the command of the one obeyed; pleasure alone does not constitute obedience.

Checkpoint
According to the first aspect, what is the defining characteristic of obedience?
A) That the doer is pleased
B) That it is done upon command
C) That it causes delight to the one being obeyed
D) That it is a physical action

Key Takeaway
Obedience is defined by acting upon command, not by the pleasure it brings to anyone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider an action you perform regularly that brings you pleasure but is not commanded by Allah. Do you ever justify it by the pleasure you get, ignoring whether it aligns with His command? What would it take for you to abandon that action if it contradicts His command?
?
Obedience, this lesson says, is defined by command, not pleasure. Is there an area of your life—like relationships, work, or worship—where you have measured obedience by how it feels rather than by what Allah has actually commanded? What is one specific change you can make today to shift your focus from feeling to command?
?
This passage forces you to examine your intentions: Are your actions done because Allah commanded them, or because they bring you or others delight? Can you think of a moment today when you chose pleasure over command? What will you do tomorrow to act solely upon His command, regardless of how it feels?

Religions Are Based on Beliefs, Not Actions
Imam Maturidi explains that religions are matters of belief, not acquired actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islam teaches that religions are defined by beliefs, not by external actions, and how a single sinful action does not alter one's religion.

Core Idea
A religion is not a list of actions; it is a set of inner beliefs.

Imam Maturidi continues refuting a question about whether a sinful action could be considered a religion because it pleases Shaytan. He provides a second answer: religions are matters of belief, not acquired actions. This lesson unpacks that distinction, showing why beliefs are beyond external coercion and how intent (qasd) is crucial.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic source passage and its literal translation. Notice how Imam Maturidi contrasts beliefs (اعتقادات) with acquired actions (أفعال تكتسب).
2
Identify the core distinction
The author states that religions are based on beliefs, not actions. Beliefs are not subject to compulsion; they are internal. Reflect on why this distinction matters for the question of whether a sin could be a religion.
Beliefs are 'actions of the heart' (أفعال القلوب).
3
Understand the role of intent
Abu Hanifa adds that the scenario (doing an action that pleases Shaytan) is only relevant regarding intent, not actual occurrence when the person does not intend obedience. Consider how intent relates to the definition of religion.
Intent (قصد) is key to judging actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثانى أن الديانات من اعتقادات لا أفعال تكتسب ، إذ الاعتقادات لا يجرى عليها القهر والغلبة ، ولا لأحد من الخلائق على اعتقاد آخر ومنعه سلطان ، ومن أفعال القلوب خاصة ، وربما كان للألسن بها تعلق من حيث لا يقدر على استعمال لسان غيره وكذلك قلبه ، ويقدر على سائر الجوارح . وإذا كانت الديانات ما ذكرنا ، والكفر والإيمان دين ، لم يصر الذي ذكرت لو كان طاعة ديناً والكفر دين ، فكيف وهو من الوجه الذى ذكرت ليس بطاعة . وقد روى عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه أجاب لهذا السؤال أن الذى ذكرته حق القصد لا حق الوقوع على حال لا يقصد ذلك ، وعلى ذلك أمور علقت بالقصد ، وذلك يخرج على ما بينا من ترتيب الاعتقادات ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And the second: that religions are based on beliefs, not on acquired actions, for beliefs are not subject to compulsion and domination. No one has authority over another's belief or to prevent it. They are specifically actions of the hearts, though tongues may have a connection to them in that one cannot use another's tongue, nor another's heart, while one can [control] other limbs. Since religions are as we have mentioned, and disbelief and faith are a religion, what you mentioned, even if it were obedience, would not become a religion, and disbelief is a religion; how can it be, while from the aspect you mentioned it is not obedience? And it has been narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) that he answered this question: 'What you mentioned is true regarding intent, not regarding actual occurrence in a state where that is not intended.' And upon that hang matters tied to intent. And that falls under what we have explained regarding the ordering of beliefs. And there is no power except through Allah.
Source pages p. 968

Commentary
This passage is a classification and argument. It states that religions (adyan) are based on beliefs (i'tiqadat), not on external actions that are acquired. Beliefs are not subject to compulsion; they are internal actions of the heart. Even if the sinful action were considered obedience (which it is not), it would not constitute a whole religion. Disbelief itself is a religion, and it is based on beliefs, not a single action. The author then cites Abu Hanifa, who said that the questioner's scenario is valid only regarding intent (qasd), not regarding actual occurrence when the person does not intend obedience. Thus, matters of faith and disbelief are tied to intent and the ordering of beliefs.

Key Terms

أفعال القلوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A single sinful action can change one's religion from Islam to disbelief.
Correction: Religion is based on settled beliefs, not on isolated actions. A sin, even if it pleases Shaytan, does not constitute disbelief unless it reflects an inner belief. Intent (qasd) determines the religious value of an act.

Checkpoint
According to the second aspect, why does a sinful action not make one a disbeliever even if it pleases Shaytan?
A) Because actions are not part of religion
B) Because religion is based on belief, not just actions, and the action is not intended as obedience
C) Because Shaytan is not a real entity
D) Because the action is always done unwillingly

Key Takeaway
Religion is defined by one's core beliefs, not by individual actions, and intent determines the religious value of an act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform acts of worship, do you ever rely on the outward action to reassure yourself of your faith, while your inner belief is weak or distracted? According to this lesson, is that enough to define your religion?
?

?

Third Answer: The Believer Overcome by Desire Is Not a Disbeliever
Imam Maturidi argues that believers who sin due to being overcome are not disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a believer who sins due to being overcome by desire or anger is not considered a disbeliever, based on Imam Maturidi's third answer.

Core Idea
Being overcome by desire does not make a believer a disbeliever if he does not intend disobedience.

Imam Maturidi presents a third answer to the question of whether believers who sin become disbelievers. He argues that when a believer is compelled by overwhelming desire, anger, or zeal, and does not intend to disobey Allah or obey Shaytan, he is like one forced. Such an action does not necessarily entail disbelief. This lesson examines this nuanced defense of the errant believer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the analogy of being 'pushed into it' (كالمدفوع).
The author uses a simile to compare the overwhelmed believer to one compelled.
2
Identify the key conditions
Find the conditions that prevent the sin from being disbelief: being overcome (غلبة), no intention to disobey Allah (لم يقصد عصيان الرب), no intention to obey Shaytan.
These conditions are central to the argument.
3
Understand the theological implication
Consider how this protects the believer's faith while acknowledging human weakness. Allah judges based on capacity to resist.
This shows mercy and justice in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا إن كل مؤمن فيها يعصى الله فى شىء يكون كالمدفوع إليه بما يغلب عليه من شهوة أو غضب أو حمية أو نحو ذلك ، وبما به يصير إليه ، إذا لم يقصد عصيان الرب أو طاعة الشيطان ، يصير من الوجه الذي ذكرت كالمدفوع ، لم يلزمه الكفر به ، والله أن يجزيه عليه بما ملكه ما به يمتنع عن الدفع إليه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And also, every believer who disobeys Allah in something is like one who is pushed into it by what overcomes him of desire, anger, zeal, or the like, and by that which brings him to it. When he does not intend disobedience to the Lord or obedience to the devil, he becomes, from the aspect you mentioned, like one compelled. Disbelief does not necessarily apply to him because of it. And Allah will reward him according to what He has given him of ability to refrain from being pushed into it. And there is no power except through Allah.
Source pages p. 969

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the errant believer. It compares the believer who sins under the influence of desire, anger, or zeal to one who is compelled. Since he does not intend to disobey Allah or obey Shaytan, he is like one forced. Therefore, disbelief does not necessarily follow from such an action. Allah will judge him according to his capacity to resist.

Key Terms

حمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Anyone who commits a sin out of desire deliberately rejects faith.
Correction: The author clarifies that when desire overwhelms and there is no intention to disobey Allah, the person is not a disbeliever.

Checkpoint

B) Because he is compelled and does not intend disobedience to Allah
C) Because desire is not a sin
D) Because he repents immediately

Key Takeaway
A believer who sins without intending to disobey Allah, but due to being overwhelmed by desire or anger, is not thereby a disbeliever.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Allah's Mercy in Not Labeling Sins as Worship of Shaytan
Imam Maturidi explains Allah's grace in not calling sins obedience to Shaytan and in promising forgiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah's mercy operates in not labeling a believer's sins as worship of Shaytan and the two ways He overlooks them.

Core Idea
Allah's mercy prevents sins from being labeled as worship of the devil.

Imam Maturidi presents a profound insight into divine mercy. He explains that when a believer sins but still hates Shaytan, Allah does not call that sin 'obedience' to Shaytan, and even promises forgiveness. This passage shows how Allah's grace lightens the burden of sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two-part structure: first the grace, then the two reasons.
2
Identify Allah's grace
The passage begins by stating that it is Allah's grace that He does not impose upon servants the label of obedience or worship to Shaytan for their sins. Recognize this as the main point.
3
Understand the two reasons for overlooking
The passage lists two reasons: (1) in this world, Allah prevents the sin from being called obedience/worship; (2) in the Hereafter, He gives hope of forgiveness because believers maintain enmity towards Shaytan.
This is the core of the lesson.
4
Reflect on the role of enmity
Notice that the believer's inherent hatred of Shaytan, even while sinning, is key to receiving mercy. This shows the importance of intention and disposition.
Contrast with someone who delights in sin and loves Shaytan.
5
Appreciate the overall theme
Consider how this teaching illustrates Allah's attribute of mercy (Rahma) and generosity (Karam). The passage ends with praise to Allah.
Think about how this understanding affects a Muslim's hope in Allah's forgiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمكن أن يقال : ذلك فضل الله إلى عباده إذ لم يلزمهم بمثل ذلك طاعة الشيطان وعبادته ، أو علم شدة ذلك عليهم على ما أكرمهم الله حال العصيان بمعاداة الشيطان وأنه لا أحد أبغض إليهم منه ولا / شيء أثقل على طباعهم وعقولهم مما فيه سرور ولذته فضلا عن طاعته وعبادته ، فتجاوز الله عنهم عن ذلك لوجهين : أحدهما في العاجل بمنع اسم الطاعة والعبادة له ، والثانى باطماع المغفرة والتجاوز بما آثر عداوة الشيطان فى وقت عصيانه رحمة رب العالمين المعروف بالكرم والجود الذى لم يزل يعودهم بإحسانه إليهم وأفضاله عليهم ، له الحمد على ذلك أوفره .
And it is possible to say: That is Allah's grace to His servants, since He does not impose upon them, by such [actions], obedience and worship to the devil; or He knows the severity of that upon them, given that He has honored them in the state of disobedience by their enmity towards the devil, and that there is none more hateful to them than him, nor anything heavier on their natures and minds than something which contains pleasure and delight, let alone obedience and worship to him. So Allah has overlooked for them regarding that for two reasons: one is in this world by preventing the name of obedience and worship being applied to him [the action], and the second is by giving hope of forgiveness and overlooking because they preferred enmity towards the devil at the time of their disobedience, as a mercy from the Lord of the worlds, known for generosity and bounty, who has not ceased to return to them with His goodness and favors. To Him be the most abundant praise for that.
Source pages p. 969

Commentary
This passage is a theological explanation of divine mercy. It states that it is Allah's grace that He does not label sinful actions as obedience or worship of Shaytan. Furthermore, Allah knows how difficult it would be for believers if every sin were considered worship of Shaytan, especially since believers inherently hate Shaytan. Therefore, Allah overlooks this in two ways: (1) in this world, He prevents the action from being called obedience or worship, and (2) in the Hereafter, He gives hope of forgiveness because the believer still maintains enmity towards Shaytan even while sinning. This is a mercy from the Lord.

Key Terms
فضل الله
مغفرة
عداوة
شيطان
رحمة
تجاوز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that sin automatically earns the label of worship of Shaytan.
Correction: The author shows that Allah's mercy prevents that label, so sins of believers are not considered worship of Shaytan.

Checkpoint
What is one of the two reasons Allah overlooks the sin of a believer who disobeys but hates Shaytan?
A) The believer repents immediately
B) Allah prevents the action from being called obedience or worship to Shaytan
C) The action is not actually a sin
D) The believer does not actually commit the sin

Key Takeaway
Allah's mercy ensures that a believer's sin, committed while still hating Shaytan, is not labeled as worship of the devil, and forgiveness is hoped for.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly feel hatred for Shaytan in your heart, or has your conscience become numb? Take a moment to ask Allah to renew that enmity within you.
?
If Allah, in His mercy, does not call your sin 'worship of Shaytan', how does that change the way you view your own failures? Will you now turn to Him with hope for forgiveness rather than despair?
?
In what specific area of your life do you still struggle with sin while feeling a deep dislike for it? Commit today to a small action that aligns with your hatred of Shaytan and your love for Allah.

The Believer's Heart Settled on Tawhid
Maturidi synthesizes the argument, stating that a true believer's actions cannot be ascribed to worship of others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a believer's outward actions do not define his religious state; rather, the settled conviction of the heart determines the nature of his actions.

Core Idea
The heart's settled tawhid sanctifies even imperfect actions.

Imam Maturidi brings the argument to a close by focusing on the inner state of the believer. He explains that once the heart is truly settled on tawhid, no subsequent action—even a sin—can be considered worship of other than Allah. This passage helps us distinguish between the believer who falters and the disbeliever whose very foundation is corrupt.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage with Attention
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how Maturidi describes the believer's internal transformation: belief, recognition, heart felt, then restraint.
The passage is dense; take your time to absorb each clause.
2
Identify the Believer's Inner State
List the elements: belief in obedience, recognition of servitude, feeling of blessings, awareness of Allah's sovereignty. See how these lead to a settled heart.
This shows the cognitive and emotional dimensions of tawhid.
3
Understand the Argument About Sin
Why does Maturidi say a believer's sin cannot be ascribed to worship of others? Find the condition: 'after his heart is settled on this.'
He addresses even when desire or hope for mercy moves the person.
4
Contrast with the Disbeliever
Note how the disbeliever's actions are linked to their false beliefs (Shaytan or self). This reinforces the principle that inner conviction grounds outer acts.
Compare and contrast the two cases.
5
Reflect on the General Principle
The final sentence introduces a principle about threatened actions: they are essentially ugly. Reflect on how this relates to the overall argument.
The text is cut off, but the idea is that the ugliness of sin is real, yet it does not negate tawhid if the heart is firm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و بعد، فإن العبد إذا اعتقد طاعة الرب ، وعرف العبودية ، وأشعر قلبه عظيم نعمه عليه وآلائه لديه ، ثم أراه عظيم سلطانه وقدرته بما ذكره حكمته في خلقه ونفاذ مشيئته فيه كف نفسه عن أن يميل إلى طاعة من لا يكون طاعته طاعته ، وصانها عن توهم عبادة دونه ، لم يجز صرف فعله الواقع منه بعد أن اطمأن قلبه على هذا ، وصير ذا آثر عنده من الدنيا والآخرة الشهوة غلبته أو لرحمة يأملها أو لأمر دفعه إليها طاعة لغيره أو عبادة منه أحدا دونه . وما ذكرته لازم قلبه وقت فعله ، وإنما يكون مثله من الكافر الذي اعتقد طاعة من دونه وعبادة من لا يستحقها أن يصرف ذلك إلى من به صار إلى ذلك من الشيطان أو النفس ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . قال الفقيه أبو منصور رحمه الله : ثم الأصل في كل شيء أوعد عليه أن حقيقة ذلك تقع من صاحبه على وجوه من القبح مما يعلم كل تفاوت ذلك في
And after that, when the servant believes in obedience to the Lord, recognizes servitude, and makes his heart feel the greatness of His blessings upon him and His favors, then He shows him the greatness of His sovereignty and power through what He mentioned of His wisdom in creation and the execution of His will in it, he restrains his soul from inclining to obedience to anyone whose obedience is not His obedience, and protects it from imagining worship of anyone other than Him. It is not valid to ascribe his action that occurs from him, after his heart is settled on this, and he considers that which is preferable to him in this world and the Hereafter, whether desire overcomes him, or for a mercy he hopes for, or for a matter that pushes him to it, as obedience to other than Him or worship of anyone other than Him. And what I have mentioned is necessary for his heart at the time of his action. And the like of this from the disbeliever who believes in obedience to others and worship of those who do not deserve it would be to ascribe that to the one through whom he came to that, whether Shaytan or the self. And there is no power except through Allah. The jurist Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Then the principle in everything that is threatened [with punishment] is that its reality occurs from its doer in aspects of ugliness, which everyone knows the disparity of that in
Source pages p. 969

Commentary
This passage is a concluding synthesis. It describes the state of a true believer: he believes in obedience to Allah, recognizes servitude, and is deeply aware of Allah's blessings and power. Because his heart is settled on these truths, he naturally restrains himself from inclining to obedience to anyone else. Therefore, even if he commits a sin due to desire or hope for mercy, his action cannot be ascribed to obedience or worship of other than Allah. His heart remains committed to tawhid at the time of the action. In contrast, a disbeliever's actions are correctly attributed to his false beliefs, whether from Shaytan or his own soul. The final incomplete sentence introduces a general principle that the reality of threatened actions is ugly, with varying degrees.

عبودية
سلطان

نفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A believer who commits a sin is essentially worshipping his desire or Shaytan because his action is wrong.
Correction: The passage clarifies that if the heart is settled on tawhid, the action cannot be considered worship of other than Allah, even if it is sinful. The intention and inner conviction matter more than the outward act.

Checkpoint
According to the final synthesis, what prevents a believer's sinful action from being considered worship of Shaytan?
A) He repents after the sin
B) His heart is settled on tawhid and he does not intend worship of other than Allah
C) The sin is not actually committed
D) He only sins in private

Key Takeaway
A believer's actions, even sinful ones, are not counted as worship of others because his heart remains firmly settled on tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you blame your desire or shaytan, or do you humbly admit that your heart's tawhid was not settled enough in that moment? What would it take for you to internalize Allah's blessings and power until your heart is truly settled?
?
Think of a recent action you performed that you later regretted. Did you, even for an instant, feel that you were worshipping your own desire? How does this lesson change your understanding of that action—does it still count as a failure of tawhid? If not, what does it mean for your repentance?
?
The believer's heart is described as 'restraining the soul from inclining to obedience to others.' Is there any area of your life where you still incline to obey people or your own whims over Allah? Will you today begin to consciously reflect on Allah's sovereignty until your heart is settled?

The Believer's Sin: Compulsion, Not Disbelief
Maturidi defines the case of the compelled believer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a believer who sins due to overwhelming desire is not considered a disbeliever or obedient to Satan.

Core Idea
When compelled by desire, a believer's sin is not worship of Satan.

Imam Maturidi addresses a subtle theological question: if a believer commits a sin because of overwhelming desire, anger, or zeal, does that count as obeying Satan? In this passage, he explains that such a person is like one compelled, and because the intention is not to disobey God or obey Satan, unbelief does not apply.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation of the first paragraph, which describes the compelled believer. Notice the key term 'al-madfu' (المدفوع).
2
Identify the condition for non-kufr
Find the phrase 'when he does not intend disobedience to the Lord or obedience to Satan'. This is the crucial condition.
3
Understand the compulsion metaphor
Reflect on the idea that the believer is 'like one compelled' (كالمدفوع). How does this affect the ruling?
Compulsion diminishes culpability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا إن كل مؤمن فيها يعصى الله فى شىء يكون كالمدفوع إليه بما يغلب عليه من شهوة أو غضب أو حمية أو نحو ذلك ، وبما به يصير إليه ، إذا لم يقصد عصيان الرب أو طاعة الشيطان ، يصير من الوجه الذي ذكرت كالمدفوع ، لم يلزمه الكفر به ، والله أن يجزيه عليه بما ملكه ما به يمتنع عن الدفع إليه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
وأمكن أن يقال : ذلك فضل الله إلى عباده إذ لم يلزمهم بمثل ذلك طاعة الشيطان وعبادته ، أو علم شدة ذلك عليهم على ما أكرمهم الله حال العصيان بمعاداة الشيطان وأنه لا أحد أبغض إليهم منه ولا شيء أثقل على طباعهم وعقولهم مما فيه سرور ولذته فضلا عن طاعته وعبادته ، فتجاوز الله عنهم عن ذلك لوجهين : أحدهما في العاجل بمنع اسم الطاعة والعبادة له ، والثانى باطماع المغفرة والتجاوز بما آثر عداوة الشيطان فى وقت عصيانه رحمة رب العالمين المعروف بالكرم والجود الذى لم يزل يعودهم بإحسانه إليهم وأفضاله عليهم ، له الحمد على ذلك أوفره .
و بعد، فإن العبد إذا اعتقد طاعة الرب ، وعرف العبودية ، وأشعر قلبه عظيم نعمه عليه وآلائه لديه ، ثم أراه عظيم سلطانه وقدرته بما ذكره حكمته في خلقه ونفاذ مشيئته فيه كف نفسه عن أن يميل إلى طاعة من لا يكون طاعته طاعته ، وصانها عن توهم عبادة دونه ، لم يجز صرف فعله الواقع منه بعد أن اطمأن قلبه على هذا ، وصير ذا آثر عنده من الدنيا والآخرة الشهوة غلبته أو لرحمة يأملها أو لأمر دفعه إليها طاعة لغيره أو عبادة منه أحدا دونه . وما ذكرته لازم قلبه وقت فعله ، وإنما يكون مثله من الكافر الذي اعتقد طاعة من دونه وعبادة من لا يستحقها أن يصرف ذلك إلى من به صار إلى ذلك من الشيطان أو النفس ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And also, every believer who disobeys God in something is like one compelled to it by what overcomes him of desire, anger, zeal, or the like, and by what leads him to it, when he does not intend disobedience to the Lord or obedience to Satan; he becomes from the aspect I mentioned like one compelled, and unbelief does not necessarily apply to him. And God will recompense him for it with what He granted him by which he could resist being compelled to it. And there is no power except through God.
And it could be said: That is God's grace to His servants, since He did not charge them with obedience to Satan and worship of him in such a case, or because He knew the severity of that upon them, as God honored them at the time of disobedience with enmity to Satan, and that there is none more hateful to them than him, nor anything heavier upon their natures and intellects than that which contains pleasure and delight, let alone his obedience and worship. So God pardoned them concerning that in two ways: one immediate, by withholding the name of obedience and worship from it; the second by giving hope of forgiveness and pardon, because they preferred enmity to Satan at the time of their disobedience, out of mercy of the Lord of the worlds, known for generosity and bounty, who has never ceased to return to them with His goodness and favors. To Him be praise for that in full.
And furthermore, when the servant believes in obedience to the Lord, and knows servitude, and his heart is imbued with the greatness of His blessings upon him and His favors, then he is shown the greatness of His dominion and power through what He mentioned of His wisdom in creation and the penetration of His will therein; he restrains his soul from inclining to obedience to one whose obedience is not His obedience, and guards it from imagining worship of other than Him. It is not permissible to attribute his action, which occurs after his heart is settled on this and after he has made that which is more preferable to him in this world and the next – whether desire overcame him, or hope for mercy, or a matter that drove him to it – to obedience to other than Him or worship of anyone other than Him. And what I mentioned is a necessary condition of his heart at the time of his action. And the like of him would only be that of the disbeliever who believes in obedience to other than Him and worship of one who does not deserve it, that his action be attributed to the one by whom he was led to that, whether Satan or the soul. And there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 969

Commentary
This passage presents a theological argument about the status of a believer who commits a sin due to overwhelming desires or emotions, such as desire, anger, or zeal, without intending to disobey God or obey Satan. The author, Imam Maturidi, argues that such a person is like one compelled (المدفوع) and is not to be considered a disbeliever (كافر) because the sin is not an act of rebellion against God or worship of Satan. God's grace is shown in two ways: first, by not labeling the act as obedience or worship to Satan in this world (العاجل), and second, by providing hope for forgiveness (المغفرة) in the hereafter because the believer's heart harbors enmity towards Satan even while sinning. The argument then examines the case of a believer whose heart is firmly settled on tawhid and servitude to God, and who then commits an act that might appear sinful. Even if such a believer succumbs to desire or hope for mercy or some external impetus, his action should not be attributed to worship of other than God because his heart is steadfast in its belief. This contrasts with the disbeliever who fundamentally believes in obedience to other than God and worships false deities; for the disbeliever, the action can be rightly ascribed to Satan or the soul. The passage thus explains the distinction between the believer's unintentional sin and the disbeliever's intentional transgression, emphasizing God's mercy and the importance of inner conviction (اطمئنان القلب).

Key Terms
كافر
المدفوع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any sin committed by a believer counts as obedience to Satan and makes one a disbeliever.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that if the sin is caused by overwhelming desire or emotion without intention to disobey God or obey Satan, the believer is not a disbeliever and the act is not considered obedience to Satan.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what must be absent for a believer's sin not to be considered disbelief?
A) The sin must be minor.
B) The believer must not intend to disobey God or obey Satan.
C) The believer must repent immediately.
D) The sin must be committed only once.

Key Takeaway
A believer who sins due to overwhelming desire without intending disobedience is not a disbeliever.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin out of a sudden surge of anger or desire, do you pause to examine your intention? Are you truly 'like one compelled', or do you knowingly indulge? Commit today to train yourself to check your heart before the act, and if you find compulsion, seek Allah's forgiveness for the weakness, not for open rebellion.
?
Have you ever looked down on a fellow believer for a sin, assuming they deliberately chose disobedience? How does Maturidi's teaching force you to reconsider? This week, when you see someone falter, ask Allah to give them strength instead of judging, remembering that only Allah knows the state of the heart.
?
Allah recompenses you according to the capacity He gave you to resist. Where in your life have you been given strength but chosen to give in? What specific step will you take today to use the strength Allah has granted you to overcome a recurring sin, rather than surrendering to the excuse of compulsion?

God's Grace: Two Ways of Pardon
Maturidi explains two ways God pardons the believer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will comprehend the two forms of divine grace by which God withholds the label of 'obedience to Satan' from a believer's unintentional sin and gives hope for forgiveness.

Core Idea
God's mercy withholds the name of sin and promises forgiveness for the believer's weakness.

After establishing that the compelled believer is not a disbeliever, Maturidi elaborates on God's grace. He explains that God does not charge such a believer with obedience to Satan, both in this world by not calling it worship, and in the hereafter by granting hope of forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
Read the second paragraph
Read the Arabic and translation describing God's grace. Note the two reasons for pardon.
2
Identify the two aspects of pardon
Maturidi mentions two aspects: one immediate (al-'ajil) and one in the hereafter (al-akhir). List them.
Immediate: withholding the name of obedience/worship. Hereafter: forgiveness.
3
Reflect on divine mercy
Consider how God's knowledge of the believer's enmity towards Satan and the heaviness of resisting desires leads to this mercy.

Faith and Disbelief
